O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and practice of the medical science, and have finished it with explanations and descriptions.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery."
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the practical art is forbidden in our region and is strange in all aspects, thus the science has perished and has been cut off, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors which have been copied by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this came the errors and false beliefs, and intentions were clouded and the science was driven away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, as well as the other instruments of the work with the addition of explanation and preparation, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no skilled masters of handiwork are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who practices (medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that he knows thoroughly about the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of them, and their movement and repose, and where they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And so Hippocrates said that a name without deeds is much, and in the art of handiwork, it is the same.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things, let him beware that he does not fall into error and kill men; just as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula or the neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; because of which so much blood flowed out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone of a watery man, and the stone was large; he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to operate on him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he were operated on, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see another physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound with bandages, and leaves no salt to the wound, and binds it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg became completely swollen and the foot came to perdition.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had undone it, he was at ease and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in any case, the corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the entire limb was lost.[](Note: The word "corruption" in this context likely refers to infection or gangrene.)
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another physician who lanced a hardened abscess, and then inflamed it further due to the malignancy of his treatment. (Note: The word "malignity" in this context may refer to the severity or virulence of the infection, or to the negative consequences of the physician's actions.)
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can completely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: that is to say, surgery where there is danger in many positions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	So take up your arms in silence, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you come to safety and are praised; and leave behind diseases that inspire dread with serious illness; and put aside your weapons from those that make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can go from this world to the other with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen said in one of his admonitions: "Do not take care of bad illnesses, lest you be called a foolish fool."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and cauteries of sharp medicine, and this chapter is arranged from head to foot; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools of cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.[ST1]
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell of the quality and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help and harm, it is the longest word and most subtle science and secret knowledge; and of this, many sages spoke and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, a hot complexion without matter, and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that cautery is of great help; and others have said the opposite: that cautery is of no value for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure illnesses caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the opposite, that cautery brings great help to hot and dry illnesses in the human body, speaks falsely.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And yet, it should not be meddled with by anyone other than the one who has tested it and is well-versed in the chapter of cauteries, as well as the diversity of human complexions, their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the outcomes and seasons; we are not afraid of other complexions, even cold and moist ones.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that fire cautery is among the treatments for curing and of greater benefit than heated medical cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is burned, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to name so.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	Heated medicines spread from one member to another and bring illnesses with difficult healing to the affected member; and perhaps kill the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this (spread illness) unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this to be true through experience and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of things. And for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for I do not wish to take away from you the secret that is hidden in fire and its quality of work, how it removes illnesses from bodies, as the philosopher says and demonstrates; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed upon a certain time for cauteries to be performed, and they chose pricking.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm arising is diminished by the aid of cautery; and even if the cauterization is necessary due to urgent and severe pain that cannot wait for the time when greater harm does not come to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as foolish men do; for the illness that is healed by cauterization does not return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not a medicine that changes complexion, and dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, rather it is a means to an end that is more effective than medicine due to its swiftness of action, and the power of its work and sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness comes at times according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its power; and excesses accumulate in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauteries for pain, and similar things, and that type of pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "derrière" (after part/hindering part) of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cautery is effective after other treatments, but their belief is false. The term "cautery is the derrière of medicine" means that when we administer methods of cures in a disease and they are not effective, we then apply cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it becomes clear that cautery is the "derrière" (after part/hindering part) of medicine, but not in the way foolish physicians think.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not become necrotic, but this is not true as I have experienced. Gold cautery is indeed more effective than iron, just as they claimed.[translation varies slightly from previous answer]
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot tell when it is hot enough by its color, which can cool down very quickly. If it is heated too much, it becomes brittle and breaks in the fire. In this way, there are many obstacles to using gold cautery.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	I have arranged this chapter from head to toe, so that the way may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery[^1^](#note-1)
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is useful for treating moisture and coldness on the brain, and there are two types of it used for a condition called "soda," as well as for various humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, causing many dreams, toothaches, sore throats, and all illnesses that result from coldness, such as paralysis, numbness, apoplexy, and similar conditions.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient must be purged with a cleansing medicine that clears the head three or four times, depending on the patient's vitality, fluids, and habits; and then let the patient's head sweat.[^1^](#note-2)
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something firm; then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come, bleed slightly, then heat the cautery called "olivary," of which this is the shape:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make downward and outward movements while pulling your hand back and forth; then quickly remove your hand, and check the mark to see if you see a small hole; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a little bit of salt, put it in wine and soft cotton, and place it on the mark, and let it stay for three days; then put dampened linen cloths with butter on top; and leave it on until the burn has healed; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacum" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer a wound stays open, the more it purges itself; and for this reason, movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some of them said that one should leave the cautery on long enough that part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caut%C3%A8re)
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that one should leave the cautery for a while, and apply it strongly enough that it makes a wound as large as a distaff that women place in their spindles so that the humors may exit; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should clean and close it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every way, except in certain men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should leave out the other one; for the head is weakened by continuous natural evacuations, as we observe in other members; and even when the head of the patient is naturally weak, and the first appearance of cauterization is more healthy and effective for me, I use this one and achieve a positive outcome.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain coming all over the head and lasting a long time, then the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and oil treatments and poultices; and if one does cauterization as we have previously mentioned, but it is not effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's condition is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize beneath the fire cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterward, make a cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery or incision in the place called "vasselz"; and it is an incision where one applies cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not see all the way to the bone: the patient feels much more severe pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of this later; and the cauteries of the horns should be finer than those used for the middle of the head, and this is the method.
dou cautere dou chief	of the head cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain comes to a part of the head and the illness extends up to the eye, and the head has been purged with cleansing medicines, and the other cures that I have said in the division of diseases have been done, and all this does not help; then one should make cauteries in two ways: namely by means of medicine and by fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medical procedure of the cautery in medicine is as follows: take a piece of aloe wood, remove the bark, and cut it into a piece to fit two fingers. Then make an incision where the pain lies, in such a way that you can place the piece of aloe wood underneath the skin; and when it is placed, bind and tighten it well, leaving it in place for twelve hours; then unbind it and remove the piece of aloe, and leave the wound open for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, apply any of the burning medicines that I have written about in the twelfth chapter on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is in the following manner. Heat the cautery to the shape depicted here:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the end is shaped like a bell with one hollowed-out curve and a small opening in the middle. Place it on the painful area and move your hand holding the iron cautery gently until half of its thickness has been burnt; then remove your hand so that the artery, which is outside and beyond, does not get burnt, allowing for the abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterwards, put cotton at the wound covered with silk, and leave it for 3 days; then put wet cotton smeared with butter, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this swelling with the cautery called "cultellare", do it at the entire tip, and take care not to cover the artery in this swelling which is not old.
de emigraine	The term "emigraine" from the original Old French text likely refers to a type of swelling or tumor. In modern medical terminology, it could be translated as "swelling", "tumor", or "growth". However, without further context, it is difficult to provide an exact translation.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure a swelling (emigraine) as we have said before in the section on diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous cautery of medicine and iron is not sufficient, then you should heat the "cultellare" cautery until it is white. And similarly place it on the painful spot, drawing a line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and pull so as not to cover the artery and reach the bone; and beware of the jaw that moves when chewing, and see that the nerve does not move and that spasm does not come upon the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut or if there is great fear in both the one who knows it and the one who does not know it, and who is not a student and experienced. And leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it belongs in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries are not sufficient for the disease and the patient is willing, then cauterize it in the same place on the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the previous one and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from part coldness
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and medical treatments and other cures as we have mentioned in the division have been attempted but the pain persists, then heat this "pointed" cautery, which has the following form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After, apply the cautery all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move it slightly above the root of the ear after you have marked the spot; and make ten cautery marks around each ear; then cure the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth[Written during a time when medical terminology used language that would now be considered harsh or inappropriate.]
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture of the mouth that should be cured by cautery is only one of those that move fluids, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.[Written during a time when medical terminology used language that would now be considered harsh or inappropriate.].
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this type of torture that moves with fluid from sweating, cleansing of the head and gargling, and if it is ineffective, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; and place the cautery on the healthy-looking part, and make the cautery next to the head of the ear slightly below the ear horn, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery in place until half of the heart is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the appearance of the scalpel that we mentioned before, but it is slightly more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after treating the wound as I said before, until it heals completely.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, but it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one at the top of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we mentioned before, and the last cautery on the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	The term "litargie" is a medieval medical term used to describe a condition characterized by vertigo or dizziness. It is derived from the Latin word "lithargyros," which means "calcareous," and was used in ancient times to refer to a type of lead carbonate that was believed to cause vertigo when ingested. In medieval medical texts, litargie often refers to a condition characterized by dizziness, disorientation, or difficulty with balance. The term may be used to describe a variety of conditions that can cause these symptoms, including inner ear disorders, neurological problems, or certain medications.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this ailment, give the patient large y ears and cleansing pills for the brain; afterward, raise the patient's head and apply to the back of the head the plaster of sinapis (mustard) that is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it (the patient) is healed in this way, that is good; and if not, perform three cauteries on the head, starting at the top and going down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would any other injury, adding to it if necessary, and if the patient is tolerant, perform one cautery in the middle; and if needed, two others on the two temples, and continue treating until it is healed; and let the cautery used be called "olivare," as I have mentioned before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coolness/coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleansed of hairs and other things as we have mentioned before; then raise the patient's head and perform cautery on the head and on each temple, and one behind and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is tolerant, and the ailment is severe, then perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and leave it until the outermost part of the burn has healed, then remove your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and use the "olivare" cautery that we mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of yeers and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, have them gargle and chew food that will cleanse the brain often with wholesome meats; then anoint the head in the middle, and perform one cautery on the vessel, and one on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able to tolerate it, perform cauteries as I have said for someone who has paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be with olive oil in the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, superfluidities or corrupt moistures and thick phlegm are present, then use such cauteries as we have said for someone suffering from paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, superfluities decline towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify the brain, as specified in the previously mentioned division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, wash the patient's head; then make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on their head; have the patient lie crosswise, and be well held in all ways; then present the liniment, and warm it with aged butter; and heat it over moderate fire, so that the forehead can tolerate it; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with other good care, until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you wish to cauterize by making multiple points across the entire cautery, this method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; and then place wet cotton in butter and chicken fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	of the inflammation of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When inflammation comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something cleansing for the head, and guard against all moisture, and make them sweat or take baths several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Afterwards, instruct them to tilt their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauterizations on the temples if the spread of inflammation is in both eyes together or in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skull with the cautery, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how to stretch it carefully, and sometimes a cautery or hot iron is made under the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	the heart of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes have become old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and one sees that it is due to cold fluids, then he should apply the cautery that I mentioned in the beginning of the chapter, descending toward the eyes: one cautery on the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries at the haiterel below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize abundantly above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the fluid inside the eyes.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you administer the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three cups of cooked wine; raise his head, and apply the middle-sized cautery on the crown of the head, and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the two eyebrows, a little below the hairline; and be careful not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis".
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the papyrus of the eye is made soft by disease and moisture, then use this cautery which is called "olivary," of which the form is as follows:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two swellings as long as they are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the papyrus is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and then cauteries are made in two ways: namely with fire or with a heated medical substance.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they (hair) grow out evenly, place the patient in your care; then on paper place a shape that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; next put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered parsley on the eye, then heat the cautery to the shape shown here:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing along the shape that you have marked many times, so that the skin is burnt evenly; and the sign of the success of the procedure is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days, then apply moist cotton in butter until the burn is healed; after that treat with ointment until it has healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then resume cauterizing in that same spot as before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural position, is even, and the hairs no longer prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cautery is what you command the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them well together; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape you have made like the fern leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in one eye only, then work on one, and if in both as well; and place wet cotton under the eye with egg white; and the patient's head should be in your care and place your hand showing above the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for they feel biting as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from the wound.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting (of the cautery) has passed, remove the cauterizing iron and check if you see the skin lifted as if it had been lifted by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not yet worked, until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then place a wet cotton compress soaked in butter on the burnt area until the burn has healed; after that, cure the wound with an ointment called "diaphoretic" and other remedies until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if you need to be careful in your work, take great care that the medicine does not get into the eyes. If the skin becomes soft and the hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area properly, just as you did before; after that, cure it until it is healed; and this is the method of treating a burn:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this, your constriction (of the eye) should be adjusted; and do not apply the same method to those who study this art (as you would to others), meaning that you should adjust your technique accordingly based on each individual's unique anatomy.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary to apply cautery to it in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and hold the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then apply a cotton swab soaked in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat the cautery tool which is parted: and place it on the head like the shape of a dove's feather quill, bring the two parts together while heating; if you wish, sharpen it from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it rounded like a tent; but in any case, this tool will be useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus and the dry matter; and if it is closed, operate on it and remove the blockage; then place hot wheat flour on the cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the white part above the eye, so that your hand does not move excessively; and place the cautery in the oil of the eye, and corrode (burn) it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization to the bone, it would be good. If not, then repeat the cautery once more, and another time if necessary, and leave it for three days; then apply a cotton swab soaked in butter, and treat the wound with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply a corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and the king according to what comes up in his chapter (instructions).
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a kind of fire cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and open the location; then place in the opening a thin piece of iron, the shape of which is as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the size of a hazelnut; and hold your hand firmly on the iron, and let the patient not move at all, lest the molten lead run into their eye; and you must place over the patient's eye cotton soaked in egg white or oil: the lead will draw out the pus from the fistula, and the healthy flesh will heal miraculously.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer a perforation to the new growth and bring the fistula back to the body of the new growth as it should be in its proper place.[∎](Note: The above translations are provided in plain text format without any additional comments or contextual information.)
des crevaices en levres	It appears that the given phrase is in Modern French and not Old French. The translation of "des crevasses en lèvres" to English is "cracks in lips".
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Much oftentimes, cracks appear on lips that are called "wrinkles," and likewise on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks, as we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small scalpel-like cautery of this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And quickly place it in the cracks until it reaches the root; after that, cover the area with a salve until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of an abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or the eye, or the palate, or the roots of the teeth, after it putrefies and rots and becomes enfeebled and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help at all: then you must have a cautery of the size of the fistula; place it on the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches the bottom of it, and the surrounding area; and do this once or twice, after the treatment of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is treated in this way, it is good; but if not, then you must reveal the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicine but it is of no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its shape conforms to the following manner: place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery as you desire; afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salt water and hold it for an hour and then spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this manner, the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is constrained, and the moisture corrupted and dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold or there is cold in the area and medical treatment does not work, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze ladle; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and soak it in boiled butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the power/strength reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see it necessary, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tooth's nerve.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, which will form as follows, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next. And it is necessary for the patient to fill their mouth with good butter in preparation for this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery to whichever side you wish, and according to what you have power over; and this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	of scrofula (a disease characterized by swollen lymph nodes in the neck)
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulous swellings are of phlegm and of cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery with a substance whose form comes after, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to its size, and leave it in place for three days; and place a wet cotton soaked in butter where the burn is, until the burn is healed; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the moistures overcome the channels of the throat, and also when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should be purged first with solving medicines; after that, perform cautery at the base of the throat, but make sure not to come too close to the throat, and only burn a little bit. After that, perform one more cautery at the joint of the neck at the top of the spine, and use the "clavicle" cautery, of which we have given the form earlier; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.

dou cautere de pleuresin	Of pleurisy cautery.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy from the roots of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly descending on the part that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining a little behind; and one in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather make it open as if you were smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And some of the ancients said that certain people use a cautery shaped like a razor and heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if done correctly, it will remove pain as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is danger and many patients die or develop fistulas that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse (or mite)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin. Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	One of these methods is to make three or four cauteries in a row, following the length of the "mice" (or mites), according to the shape of the liver cautery that we have mentioned before; and do not press your hand on all of the cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back.[

de ydropisie	of dropsy

The fire cautery is of no use to a dropsical patient, except for the method called "asclytes". When you cure them according to the methods we have mentioned in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries around the belly, one on the stomach, one on the liver, two behind the back near the spine, and one next to the ribcage; and let the cauteries be close to the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the cautery on to remove decay for a long time, and do not stop caring for the patient after the cautery; and if sanitation is hurried, both intentions will be combined with the help of God.

The shape of the cautery for the stomach should be like a claw, as we have shown before; and the one for the back should be olive-shaped, as it is described above.
de l’enfleure des piez	of swelling in the feet

de la cure des emorroydes	Here is a line-by-line translation of the medieval medical treatise about the cure for hemorrhoids:
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: .iij. sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et .i. cautere desoz la boude. ij. dois;	When hemorrhoids are in the rectum, one or more, and they are old and consist of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and have been treated as we have said in divisions, but to no avail, then cautery should be applied: three on the spine of the back, that which is completely outside, below the dimple of the buttocks, arranged in a triangle, and one cautery beneath the haunch. Two fingers width [from the anus].
et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on .i. grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et .i. autre sus le foie, et i. autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you think that his stomach is cold and food does not cook, and the face appears swollen, then apply one large cautery to the stomach, as has been said before, and another to the liver, and another to the spleen with a clavicle-shaped cautery; and leave the cautery open for a long time. Afterwards, cure the wound until it is healed.[Note: The translation "and the face appears swollen" is an interpretation of the old French word "faice", which can also mean "cheeks".]
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy part which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the "thelul," heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it all heated upon the cut "thelul;" and leave your hand there until the cauter reaches the base of the vein, causing the blood to flow; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of "thelul," cauterize each one as we have said; after that, apply wound treatments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchemy, it will be of greater help.

de la maladie des reins	of the kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide. de la vessie	of the bladder.
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then perform cautery on the outer side of the bladder in the area where the pubic hair begins, one on each side, with each cauterization as long as the width of a coin; and perform one cautery on the back, or two if necessary; and let them be clavicle-shaped, according to the form described earlier.
