de la hainche	Of the swelling/inflammation. The word "hainche" is derived from the Old French word "enflence" which means swelling or inflammation.
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the case of the swelling/inflammation, and for this reason it moves from its place, and one of the signs is that the thigh appears longer than the other when measured together; and if the location of the separation is visible, then you must cauterize the patient on the case of the swelling with a cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the separation around the case as it turns, so that the case is within the circle; and let the cauteries be similar to those used for cauterizing the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not present, then make three cauteries from olive oil, and let them be as deep as the heart; and heal it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the groin/hip girdle
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain occurs in the hip girdle's case/box (groin) and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated for what was said in the division (treatment) and the cure is unsuccessful, and the illness is chronic: then you must purge the patient of heavy humors with fetid pills or other similar good-working pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	Afterward, perform the fire cautery; and there are two manners of cautery: namely, hot medicinal concoctions and fire cautery. Fire cautery has many forms, one of which is as follows: cauterize on the hip girdle's case/box (groin) three triangular cauteries according to this form, making them deep and large, and with a space the width of two fingers between each cautery; and let the cauteries be oval-shaped. Sometimes a single cautery is performed in the middle on the top of the hip, creating four cauteries arranged like this:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. And this is the method used in sciatica when pain persists in the hip but does not reach either the thigh or the leg. If the pain extends to the thigh and leg, perform two cauteries where the patient indicates the pain, and one cautery above the ankle, four fingers wide, slightly to the left; let the cautery be sharp, and let all excess flesh be burned. Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, do more; and if you know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, perform fire cautery using a scalpel-shaped or circular cauterizing iron, and take great care in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on for so long that you burn the nerves and major arteries, and do not cause further harm and contraction to the patient.

Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort. Heat the iron until it is all red and begins to drip molten material, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, rotating it on the healthy side. de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from percussion (striking), or from excessive evacuation, or from the spreading of cold matter, no kind of cautery is effective for these conditions, except in the case of that which results from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after this, the patient be purged with foul-smelling pills or other similar substances, and then three lines of incense marks should be made on their back, where the pain persists, using a compass; and in each line there should be five cauteries or more, depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be done using the type called "poins" (points); and if you wish, do three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle using this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often occurs in young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find at the base of the spine on the back, and appearing above the other vertebrae, an abnormal growth.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this [thing] and wish to cure it, cauterize it with a fire-hot iron in this manner.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine, heat it up evenly. And if you see pus, cauterize around the spine with a pointed iron, leaving a gap of two or three lines between the cauterization points. Ensure that the points are close to each other. de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints is due to moisture spread throughout every member of the body, and when it comes to the feet, which is called "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if it is necessary to apply the iron to the sole of the foot, make a cautery on the entire surface that is called "point". And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, and this happens often, make three or four cauteries on each knee on all sides, using an olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not keep your hand far from the heat of the fire.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the arms, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the legs or up to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicine. For if you take good care of them and purge fluids, they will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the opening (or incision) of the abscess.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see to cure it, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly, so that feces descend from their belly; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess subsides, and press it with your fingers, and place a bandage under the incision on the bone of the wrist, and in such a way that it forms half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	until it is white and exudes pus. Then press the bowels back to their place; and the attendant should place their hand so that they do not return; and work well on the thighs of the patient, and place a cushion and a sergeant (assistant) on the thighs, and another on the chest who holds their hands; then place the cautery on the mark with your whole hand, and hold it directly and firmly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you come to the bone; and be careful that the abscess does not burst when you apply the cautery; that you do not burn them; and so that through this the patient does not die, or suffer any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be fine according to the measure of eggs, and also large for larger people according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is removed; after curing with other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the boils do not come out when he takes exercise in chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and have him wear it for forty more days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not exert himself too much and be wary of overconsumption of drink and food, and of speaking excessively; and when he follows this teaching, he will be completely healed. And I will speak later about the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Here is the translation of the given Old French text:
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known (identified), and you see that they do not grow anymore, then perform one cautery with the reusable cautery, according to its size; and let it be burned one third of the stomach; after cure as we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-pronged cautery in this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	but sign first the joint's location and make a mark along the width above the rupture, and another below, and place your hand in the middle of the entire fire-hot iron. But the first cauterization is lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in some limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to a limb, either from falling or being injured, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it should be cauterized with the "point" cautery, and the cautery should be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and power, and its location in terms of twists and pain. If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for it is customary for it to change to the nearest member, so you should continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. When you see it necessary to cauterize, pay attention if the disease is in its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not worsen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the patient's body, then do five cauteries on the head: one on the crown, and another at the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two temples, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and so much that the skin comes out, allowing the vapors of the thick humors to escape; and cauterize on the wound according to what it is beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the symptoms are spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery in the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the thighs of the hips, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollow of the hands; and beware of nerves that are at the rear pressing on the heels, so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one another on the bone of the stomach, and one another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more cauterization you do, the more benefit it brings and it helps; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary for the cauteries to be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the forms of irons. Afterwards cure the place with flour of vetch and honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	I'm not sure what you mean by "de enfleure." If you are asking for a translation, "enfleure" could be translated as "swelling" or "inflammation" in English. However, without more context, it is difficult to provide a precise translation.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices but does not heal, then cauterization should be done on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cautery be a little into the thickness of the flesh; then cure it with dressings until it heals. And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should attempt this if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	of ulcers/sores
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has awakened, and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery somewhat deeply, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and one part each of swine blood and pigeon blood; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and leave it in the air until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	curing cancer/chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When cancer/chancre comes at the beginning and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a circle, all around the cancer/chancre. And yet wise men say that one should also perform cauterization in the middle of the cancer/chancre; but this does not seem good to me at all, because I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen several times; and a more correct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circular", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot mature/ripen
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in killing or through the excess fluid it makes, or due to the water of the sick person when they are very old (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you want to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards, leave it like that. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you want to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery until it is red-hot, like this:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the bone, and make sure that the cauteries are such that the patient feels them from outside in a way that alleviates the course of decay. Then cure it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the healing/curing through fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another kind of illness there is, called "corrodens", which is nothing other than an eating away at the member, for it eats away at the members as fire consumes dry wood. If you see this illness in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cautery iron very gently and large, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then let it rest for three days, and put on the burned places crushed herbs with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all of the corruption. After this, cure it with ointments that generate flesh. And if after three days you see that healthy flesh has not arisen, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on those parts of the corrupted place that remain. And this eating away has sometimes been cured by a water-based medicine instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for water-based medicine in the division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of fungi that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	It often happens that on the feet there arises an illness which is called "clos" in our language, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this illness is of two kinds: namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is as follows: heat up one iron pin as if it were a roof tile, and make it of good metal and of a size that can grasp the nail from all sides, and let it have thin edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until you reach the base of the nail; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then make an ointment of wild malva crushed with oil, and leave the ointment on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with a flesh-generating ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are turned inward on the body, and this happens frequently both in hands and feet, then one must apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a cane of iron or copper, or a roof tile pin, and place it on the nail and the warts, that is to say, fungi; and put the cane on top so that it covers all around, then add some hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the nail, and so that the hot water can find a deep path to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will detach itself along with all its roots. Do this one after another, until you reach all those on the body, then cure them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	the treatment of trembling/shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from coldness of the nerves, or quartan fever or another, then you should apply to them 4 cauteries or 4 on the spine along the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery or piece on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling, and hasten the recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes foul pustules appear on the body, caused by thick corrupted matter. In such cases, when they first appear, it is necessary to apply a cautery on each pustule: use a slender probe made from myrtle wood, with its tip heated in fire, or a root of aristolochia, or a round-shaped cautery. Sometimes, they are cauterized at the beginning, according to this method, and they cannot grow any further; instead, their superfluities are ruptured, and they heal; however, it is essential that this be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	when an artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are heavy bleedings of blood from the cut artery that spread outward, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cauterization of a limb, and in similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, you must quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips from it; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both large and small, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, according to the wound and the place where the artery is cut, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it starts to bleed again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, take another one quickly from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and make sure that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four means that we have mentioned: either with a cauter, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or with medicines applied to it that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will treat tight constriction with bandages or place hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it. (My translation)
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone who does not have any remedy or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it out until it is tightened over the wound and the vein; and must not move it, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and swollen and tightened; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases for which it is necessary to use fire cautery or a hot medicine, and we have described the instruments and forms of cauteries; and I have arranged this chapter from head to toe, and in this chapter, I will proceed in the same manner so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this, it is appropriate, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to undertake foolish things. For many kinds of people come for cures, some of whom are so afraid of their illness that they easily die from the violence they find in their disease and the severity of its harm; and these should be feared.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And among these there are those who regain their strength and say: "wait, I am healed"; but the illness is contemptuous. One should by no means agree to those who come to you with this attitude, but rather place greater emphasis on your honor than on your greed, and do not foolishly open up for those about whom you are uncertain and from whom you cannot gain both profit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the care of your patients so that health may be restored; and this will help you to establish a good reputation, and glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear son, may Our Lord give you understanding and correctness, and if you wish to inspire of the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	I have divided this chapter into sections for you, as it is in the chapter on cauteries that I have previously described, from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often occurs in children during childbirth, and when the birth is difficult and the mother squeezes the child's head too hard; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw this disease except in children, and in all those that I have seen, death came quickly; and for this reason, it seems better to me to abandon the treatment in such cases.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child where the head was full of water, and the neck swelled each day so that it could no longer support itself; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is collected under the skin on the neck between the throat and the bone; and the treatment is such if the moisture is between the throat and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the middle of the neck a finger's width long; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture can run out; and behold the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see the signs that the corners of the mouth are open on both sides, and the water jumps out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not heal; then you must make three incisions in the middle of the neck in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all pus; Afterward, bind the wounds with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then undo the binding, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and continue to bind the head as well, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is to look where the swelling of the abscess is most prominent and where the water has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Incise then where the abscess is most prominent and where the water has gathered, and make an incision according to what you have the power to do; and be careful not to cut an artery; and if a flow of blood comes, so that the patient dies from bleeding and evacuation of pus.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a person gets a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or in the groin, and the illness is chronic, and medical treatment does not help at all, then the last resort is the cautery with which one will burn two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you burn the eyes, it is necessary that the patient bend their head back; after that, rub the area around it with a rough cloth until the arteries appear; then have the patient stretch out their neck with one cloth; then look for where the veins bulge, and they are located one on each side of the ears, and are slightly sunken; then mark the spots with ink; then burn one and the other with a sharp spatula in two parts until the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done across the forehead.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver. Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, blood will spurt out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the touch, you should measure a quantity of three fingers' width, then make an incision down to the bone; and that which needs to be let out of the blood is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can withstand and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if pus remains on the tip of the syphac, cut away so that pus does not come back, then close the wound and bind it, treating it with ointment until it heals.

Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old migraines come, and acute catarrh, due to moisture of tears and heat in the temples and swollen, crazy ancient forehead and similar things, and it is treated by various medical cures but none of them help, we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is as follows: the patient should shave the hairs of his temples and pay attention to the artery that appears in the temple, for it can be easily seen by its beating, and is not very prominent except in some men who are too cold; and if it is hidden, let the patient strain his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and apply warm water to the area until the artery becomes clearly visible; then take an instrument of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with hemostats, and carefully separate it from the membranes that are beneath it on each side; and if the arteries are fine, then hook them with the tip of the forceps, then cut that part according to the quantity of the two holes. For if it is not cut, the blood will not escape at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	and draw blood from the six holes, up to three; and if the arteries are large, then it should be tied in two places with a strong double thread of silk, so that there is no putrefaction before the wound heals, and bleeding comes; then cut the excess that is between the two ties at that very hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize the remaining part with the surgical cautery up to the bone until the holes are closed; and this is the more difficult task, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is a remedy to end moisture: for this reason, it is of greater help with moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	And for the extraction of arteries, it is necessary to fill the wound with old cotton and apply well-made bandages; and when they are loosened, cure with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it heals; and if an artery is cut during the procedure, hurry to close it with a cautery, or use a vitriol-filled wound and press on it with your hand until the bleeding stops; and if you don't have this on hand, place your thumb on the wound until the blood clots, and pour cold water over it until it stops, and press as needed; and the more difficult and lighter task in extracting an artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of two parts, but make sure the edges are thick so that they maintain heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and when you have marked the two places, place your heated iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be far apart because this fire cautery is not solid all around; and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Of tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears are flowing from the veins that are above the forehead and no medicine helps, and you see the face of the patient become red, and feel a pulsation on the forehead like a trembling; and if the eyelids are tight and moist so that the paper has fallen off, and the papers have been warmed up and scorched by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is required. (Note: I am assuming "des larmes" in the first line refers to the flow of tears or excessive tearing)
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And it was called by the ancients "cure contuse", and what you should do is shave the patient who has this illness's hair on their forehead, then make three incisions on the forehead equally according to its length; and let one of the incisions be in the middle of the forehead going downward until just above the nose, and the other two at the temples above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are located above the eyelids; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two mandibles (jawbones), and let each wound be the width of three fingers across joined. (Note: I am assuming "des larmes" in the previous text refers to the flow of tears or excessive tearing)
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and much cloth to wipe away the blood, then apply the following mixture, made from two parts of:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision at the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the flesh that is between the two cuts right up to the sinciput (scalp tissue) above the bone. Then do the same thing from the middle incision to the other second one, after which extract this mixture.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	place in the first incision the instrument called "culterelle," which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other. This is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place the sharp edge of the scalpel towards the fleshy part of the skin and the blunt side towards the bone, pushing it until it reaches the middle incision. Cut all the blood vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous down to where the flesh can be seen, then do the same thing in the second incision. Equally drain the blood, squeeze out any remaining and place a piece of old cotton in each incision. Place damp cloths soaked in wine, oil, and vinegar on top and ensure that no pus forms. On the third day, loosen the bandages and apply a large amount of cold water, followed by a basilicon ointment with rose oil, as well as other treatments used for wound care until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the swelling of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone is accustomed to getting a catarrh, and you see the eyes sunken and small, with weakened vision, and inflamed eyelids; and the hair falls out, and there is deep pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those matters and those catarrhs do not come from one vein alone, and the proper cure for it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And it is necessary for you to instruct the patient to bend their forehead, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another one about an inch wide. Begin the incision from the left temple to the right temple, and let it reach the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move while eating; once the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate the two lips of the incision and place a piece of old cotton, and bandage with linen cloth; then apply dampened bandages on it with wine and oil, and be careful not to cause a hot abscess; once removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that help the flesh to heal.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make it into an ointment; and apply it to these wounds to help the flesh grow throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of stuffing the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains or an animal or a stone from mines or similar things such as iron; or seed such as lice, beans, peas; or fluid such as water and mucus and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When something falls into the ear such as a stone or any other thing that does not fit well in the ear or grow in the ear, then expose the ear to sunlight. If you see the stone, apply a few drops of violet oil or wormseed oil, then facilitate extraction; make them sneeze using condiments, and block their nostrils when they sneeze, and place pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and pull upwards on the ear. This cure often works; and if it does not work, use subtle forceps, of which this is the shape:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a fine hook made of thin double-wire; and if it does not come out this way, then make a small silver tube and insert one end into the ear canal, stopping up the area around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull strongly, because often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, then take birdlime, place some on an instrument suitable for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it [the abscess] does not come to a head with all the things we have mentioned, then hurry to lance the ear so that pus and swelling may come out, and the manner of lancing is as follows: first make the patient recline, then bleed them from the head, drawing blood according to their strength. Then have the patient sit between your hands, turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area; let the incision be crescent-shaped, continuing until you reach the bone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck out the pus with your mouth; treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a hard grain that has formed and it swells, then perform an extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply a thin suppository of this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	and make an incision of that grain. But do not do this when you think the grain is moist due to moisture in the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then carefully extract it with tweezers and suck it out gently, as we have said, so that the extraction may be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should use expectoration with mild condiments first, and fill the ear with cotton. Let them lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this means, that is good. If not, then take many small and light pebbles, heat them slightly in the fire, and place one or two of them in the patient's ear canal and jump up and down on one foot while striking the outside of the ear with another stone. Continue to do this until all of the water has come out, and then it will be completely removed. And if you wish, take a reed and insert one end into the ear, lighting the other end on fire until the inner part is burned; repeat this process with other pieces of reed until all of the water has come out, as we have said in the previous method with stones.[Original text has some inconsistencies and repetitions which have been maintained in translation for accuracy.].
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then arrange for a gradual extraction with tweezers; and this is one of the easier things to remove that can be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ear, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in the section on distillations, and the treatment does not work, then look at the ear in the sunlight: if you see any worms, remove them with fine tweezers, and if you don't see any, take a piece of straw such as this (...);
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow below and wide above. Insert the thinnest end of the straw into the ear according to the severity of the patient's discomfort, then pull the entire straw out; do this frequently until all the worms come out. If they don't obey by coming out, plug the straw with cotton as I have said in the section on stones; and if they still don't come out as we have described, administer the distillations that have been proven effective in the elimination of worms, which you can find in the section on distillations; and then drip your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, such as this (...).
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or brass, narrow below with a small hole, and wide at the top for distillation; and have a well-made brass instrument to press the distillation inside, and if you want, take a funnel and wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you wish of your medicines into the straw, which should be in the ear; then insert the funnel with all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or flows from the ear; and let the patient smell it inside, and let the distillation be a small bag heated by fire so that it can be distilled into the ear; and make sure that it's not too cold, as the medicine would not be effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have any holes in the ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to stopping up of wounds or pus inside the ear, and these stoppings occur sometimes deep within the ear, so that they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small pocket at the entrance of the hole, and it can be seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The one that occurs deep within and cannot be seen is of difficult healing in many cases, and for the one that can be seen, you should place the ear of the patient towards the sun; and look inside: if you see an apparent blockage, then work on it using this method:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and blunt both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is due to pus or flesh in the ear, then hold it with fine tweezers and gently squeeze, until all the flesh is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the blockage is deep within the ear, then take a fine and sharp razor, heat it slightly by fire, and place it in the ear canal. If you feel the blockage, which causes discomfort to the patient upon hearing, make a small incision but be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.[1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egyptian_ointment)
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder of vitriol ground up; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding comes, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that remove the bleeding which are in the treatment of distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the flesh of the papers (not sure of this translation, it could mean "pulp from paper" based on context)
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelu (comfrey) that comes in papers for the eyes when they are moist and dry, you must stretch them with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it is not cut out, cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and after the incision, the cauterizer must move; and they often heal, as long as something remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, those roots are burnt and do not return at all.
de la gresle	Of hail or a hailstone.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times there come on paper from the eyes things that resemble hail in their shape and hardness, and for this reason, this illness is called "gravel" (or literally "hail"), and it is a gathering of thick moisture in the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: take care if the gravel moves from one side to another, and this is easy to notice; then make an incision on each side, then gently scrape each part, then take it with forceps and cut it. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper a little, do not worry about the patient; and if the wound is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not apply any pressure, because ointments quickly restore it and improve the flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper and hold the gravel with forceps, and cut it and press it from one side and the other; and if the paper is separated by incision, do not worry about it; and once the gravel has been removed, rinse the eye with salty water, and cure the wound of anything that harms the flesh until the patient heals.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.
