Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is instilled on paper sheets and this happens more in children than in any other people, and it greatly harms their eyes, and they have discharge in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and therefore, they lie down on their faces and sleep on it, and their papers are moist under their eyebrows which swell and have the appearance of exinach which is visible in the eye. And when you press the area around it with your fingers, you can feel the exinach coming out.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of the procedure is as follows: the patient places their head over your sanctioned area; and then take a linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the amount of exinach present in each part, then place it on top; and press with your fingers from one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the center; then make an incision in the middle of the wet area with a spatula-shaped instrument, and it should not be any larger than the wound made when opening a vein; and cut through the skin until you reach the exinach; and in multiple ways, exinach comes out of the incision, in the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then pull out all of it with a piece of cloth between your fingers and turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed; and be careful not to press too hard on the incision, not to reach the whole spatula-shaped instrument to the eye, so that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the incision does not appear at the beginning of the cut, slightly increase the cut lengthwise until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in oil and water, and place them on the wound, and bind it with strips.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who crush soil and place it on (the wound) to corrupt the moisture that has remained, then cure it until it is healed. And if a hot abscess comes to the surface, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of the paper (shavings)
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper shavings other than those which are natural are born, and they become ingrown and reach the eyes, they harm the eyes and bring about various types of illnesses such as watery eyes and swelling of the eyelids and cloudiness, to the point where it is the cause of eye destruction. And the cure for this is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine which is appropriate according to what is before the chapter on cautery, and is done either by incision and suture or by caustics, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, insert a needle with a single thread attached; and let this be beside the edge of the paper where the hairs grow next to the lashes, and pull the thread over the entire paper, and turn it to the cutter; then make an incision beneath the paper, close to the eyelashes, the entire width of the eye, from the outer canthus to the inner canthus; then remove the thread and place a small cotton and linen tent underneath the paper, then place a figure of a prop, such as a myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the figure matches the height you intend to raise the paper which is determined.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is need to cut a large portion of the eyelid according to how soft the eyelid is; then make an incision the entire width of the eye along the two lines that you have marked, and begin at the outer canthus and continue to the inner canthus; and let one of the cuts be close to the natural lashes, as thick as a root, then insert the needle into one of the angles of the eyelid, then remove the skin; then bring together the two edges with a stitch of a needle with one thread of fine wool, and wipe away the blood, and apply some sticky substances to the excess threads on the eyebrows if you wish to do so; and if not, then pay it no mind, then leave the stitches and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitches using drying and constricting substances, for the eyelid will heal on its own at the site of the wound and bring the edges together, but stitches are harmful (as the ancients have said), and this is a fearless operation.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And there is another way: and it is that you mark the eyelid with a figure in the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have described, with three incisions unseparated according to the form which is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut away what is above with small forceps according to the form which is shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the strength to hold the pincers, and the thing is not even, take a needle with a thread, and place it in the middle of the wound; and put another thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and align the threads evenly between your fingers; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin that you have marked, as we have told; then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with a plaster and similar calming ointment.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And it sometimes happens that the hairs of the paper are turned inward: then you must do as we have said about the incision, but stitching in one and the other is more technical.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of veins is as follows: and it is that you turn the paper inward and make two incisions by art, and two fine ligatures as long as the paper and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two ends of two parts where you hold the threads; then join them subtly on top of the part of the paper over the eye, and pull firmly the two veins from both sides; and leave it like that for several days, and the skin that is pulled will die and turn black and rot, so that it falls through it.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, cut deeper, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is healed, and if the paper rises up, and the hairs no longer prickle; and this is the form of the two veins that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	the work is such that you take a thin needle and put in it one thread of soft and thin silk; then join the edges and tie them together delicately, and let the length of the threads be a palm long; then place another delicate thread of silk in the groove and tie the ends of the thread; then have the patient place his head in your lap; and be beside the sun so that the work is well-lit, for it is a delicate and fine job; then insert the needle into the entire groove at the root of the adjusted hair, and make it pierce through the paper quickly until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull out the hair up to the groove, and put that hair in the groove, if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand so that all the hairs come out at the entire groove on the paper along with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the groove is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, then you will pull the groove from underneath the entire length of the thread that you have placed in it, until the groove comes out of the opening above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the groove and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and new skin grows over it; and if the hairs are small, then attach one long hair from natural eyebrows and lift it up with that or let it be lifted up until it is lengthened, and then tie it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the decay or putrefaction of the eye. The phrase "de la porriture de l'oeil" can be translated as "of the decay or putrefaction of the eye." It is not clear from the provided text how this condition relates to the instructions given, but it seems that it may be a complication or concern in the context of treating the eye.
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the decay, comes to the eye, it can happen in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It can occur suddenly due to a wound, a cut, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of the treatment is that you split that suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages in it, and bind it until it has healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying and constricting substances in its cure. For if you do so, the illness will return worse than before; but rather use softening substances, such as fenugreek; and let water or ale and flaxseed be cooked, and let oil-based ointments be melted in one of the oils, and wrap a bandage around it, and cure it with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you take care that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and these treatments that we have mentioned are only adjustments for this illness, so that it does not return to its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is beneath (the eye) which is truly called "axacrati", and it is both natural and accidental. The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; and the way to work on it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and insert it into the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the skin above along the entire needle, and stitch it with a spatula-shaped instrument.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the form of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the crease, and turn the paper, and make two creases along the inside of the paper; and let the corners of the two creases be at the two angles of the incision you have made, and make them meet so that the form is like the form of a letter called "j greek"; then remove the flesh according to the amount by which its sides are uneven below the paper, then join the two separated parts and sew them together with a thread of wool; then treat it with the medicines we have mentioned, softening and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a wound, suture or cautery, you must make an incision in a clean line through the skin of the paper as described above; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage as I have said; and perform the work according to the form of the illness, for it is diverse in form, and wise masters should prepare means with all their power to make the form return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, depending on what is required in terms of work and instruments, can adapt to multiple dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens to many people in such a way that the paper on top is glued to the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch the eyelids with forceps until you cut the very thin skin that is not raw, without being too sharp or cutting too much, so that the patient can endure it and the thin skin is not too sharp to hurt the eye. And make your incision lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and clean the whole wound, and at times put in salty water, and remove the water with sweet collyrium (a powder used as a lotion); then place a linen bandage between the paper and the eye, and place wool soaked in egg on the eye; and after three days use collyrium and other remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the toe of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the cuticle (ongle) is of two kinds: one is nervous and resembles a hard callus, and another that is not nervous but rather resembles congealed white mucus, which cannot be touched with iron and pinched; and both appearances begin near the outer corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye and all its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is as follows: the patient places their head in your lap, then you open their eyes. Lift the paper with your hand, and use tweezers to pull the cuticle upward. Then take a needle and attach a horsehair or cow hair to it using strong thread, and insert the needle into the cuticle, piercing through completely. Attach the cuticle with thread and stretch it upwards. Then carefully remove all the hairs on the side of the cuticle that follows the eyelid and lashes up to the brow, cutting the remaining skin at the root near the outer corner of the eye using a sharp scalpel or small forceps, leaving the natural cartilage or eyebrow intact so as not to damage the tear duct. Sometimes, the cuticle extends only to the eyelash line and not beyond it, as we have mentioned; then, remove only the excess skin around the eyelashes with a soft scalpel as follows:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to let the scalpel touch the fleshy tissue and break it, or damage the oil glands. After making the incision, put a little bit of crushed salt and collyrium (an eye medication made from antimony) into the eye, and leave it there until the next day. Then treat the eye as necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not sensitive, and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this similar condition of a nail is often cured with medicines; and they come to a head as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, let the patient's eye look at it, and take the spatula, not too sharp, according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And raise the nail gently from above, and if you see that it does not diminish and the pus approaches, distill from your mouth into the eye a collyrium made of litharge and red cinnabar and oil, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, such as a developing abscess, then lactate it, and first treat the hot abscess until it heals, then resume the work as before, until it heals.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid interferes with the eye by causing significant harm, then suspend it at the base, and remove a portion of it but not all of it, so that tears can still reach it; then distill into the eye a red collyrium made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Sometimes a red flesh grows over the pupil in some men's eyes, covering the pupil and turning it to the inside, appearing like a rose baluster; and the procedure is that the patient puts his head over you, then you open his eyes and remove all that flesh with suitable hooks held tightly; then cut the first flesh, continuing to cut with the razor until the end, making sure not to wound the eye during the procedure; and let the incision be with the spatula that we mentioned in the incision of the nail and small fractures from which one removes pus, as shown in the following form after this chapter.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, then apply the eye with a mixture of crushed eggshell or where you distillate red bile and similar corrosive medicines; and put cotton outside the eye with an egg white coating, so that it is secured against hot abscess; and if there remains anything, and pus overflows, and you suspect hot abscess, then leave the eye and cure the hot abscess with calming remedies; then return to your work until it heals, and do the same when flesh has been joined in the eye by this method.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	Nevertheless, it is necessary to lighten the treatment of each weak eye by natural means; and in case of an accidental injury, with surgical methods; and never put your hand in any of these procedures until you see that this member can endure the procedure.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	These are red veins that are located over the eye and interfere with its function and weaken the eye all days. Therefore, it is necessary to first examine if the eye has any other ailment except for these veins; then, treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy side, then gently pull those veins to the very end according to your knowledge and skill, and make sure that the pulling is done with fine doubles according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two loops in one piece according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and then carefully pull those veins with force, and wipe the blood little by little until you see the veins move out of the eye; and make sure that you do not poke the eye with the tips of the spatulas, and perform this task at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only pull on those veins; and once you have done this, instill a mixture of green and red bile into the eye to destroy any remaining residue from the veins.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you are not able to gather all of it in that hour, then apply a plaster on the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain subsides and is free from hot abscess; then start again according to the method described earlier until it heals; and this is the form of treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The experts call a fistula of the eye an "arissati": when you cure it by cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is deception in that you should lance on the abscess where it should burst, and draw out all the moisture that is in it until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see the corruption and blackness, then take all the instruments that are in this form; and it is called an "aspre chief", and it should be made with a iron resembling a half-moon, pointed like a file as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the "aspre chief" on the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers and press down with your hand a little until you know that the corruption has been removed; and do this several times, then restore the layer of drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the layer is attached and flesh has grown, and the flesh of the wound is healed, and it remains so for 40 days without becoming inflamed or infected, then you know that it is healed; if not, there is no other option but to return the fistula to the opening of the nose according to this form: and that is to uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with hot medicines, and when it is exposed, take a "foret" of this form, and let the iron have three angles, and let the rod be made thin at the end as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone next to the cheekbone, and move your hand away from the eye by about a finger width, then turn the entire tool until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it as they will if they hold their hand over their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh comes out and hardens the place, then the matter goes to the nose; this makes it an easier task for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the eye socket
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open wide without any disturbance or decrease in vision, then you should bind the patient; then cleanse it, then apply suction cups or leeches without striking, then place on the eye a bandage made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then compress the eye, and dress it with cloths and bandages; and the type of cloth should be soft enough, and fold each one in four layers, and then put one over the other according to the quantity needed for the eye; then bind it firmly with a bandage and renew the suction cups without striking; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye compressed day and night, and if the bandage softens, then you must tighten it; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then renew the dressing and cloths and bandages and bandage until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of retinal detachment.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the grown eye, then it opens and comes out like a grain of resin, and is frightening to see; if you see such a sight, the procedure is as follows: take a needle and stick it into the root of the lower part up to the upper part, then put another needle where there is a double thread from the outer corner; and make it pierce, leaving the first needle in place according to the disposition; then cut the loose end of the doubled thread and tie one part of the eye around it, and bind it tight, then remove the needle and place a raw egg yolk soaked linen on it; and leave it until the threads stick to the eye, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; and sometimes the wound is bound by the eye with a circle of cloth until it heals.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye appears swollen, then pierce it with a fine spatula that comes from deep within the eye, and let the watery humor run out and make the eye descend and enter quickly; then remove it until it heals.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bow of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a bow (swelling) gathered in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of this appearance is that you make the patient sit on an appropriate and straight chair, then hold their head with both hands and turn it until you see the swelling come above your eyes; then let it be stuck (pierced) and do not let the light descend and fall, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not go down, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not prepared as we have said: then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and make an incision in the cornea with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal tissue and the ring, until the swelling goes out; and when it has gone out, distill warm water mixed with honey into the eye, or water or fenugreek boiled with honey, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the waters/humors of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	We have similar waters/humors in the division, and what is required to pierce them; and we work according to the health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from light for the sun, and bind the healthy eye very tightly; then place the paper on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the thickness of a hair in that whiteness of the eye at the side of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand until it pierces in the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda is at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the horned tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it down under one way after another. If the water comes out now, let the patient look at what is before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest, and if the water rises again in the second duct, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and no longer rises, gently remove the almagda by turning your hand slightly; then put a little bit of gemstone seal on the eye and raise it inside. Then place over it cotton or wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white, and bind it with the healthy eye. We, and those who are of our time, place above it common bread soaked with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then only pierce the ligament, and do not go too deep, but make a shallow incision, then put in almagate, as we have said; and at the completion of the task, prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping aid, in which they sleep on their back in a dark room; and be devoid of all movements, and partake light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and make him see some things, and then replace the binding until the seventh day; and it is not at all necessary that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you lighten this, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If an abscess is about to come, you shall unbind the eye before the seventh day and direct it towards what soothes abscesses; and when it has calmed down, then unbind the vision and place on its edge a bandage to cover for some days, and always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house little by little and gradually return to your usual activities; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And then came to us someone who was from Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almagate by piercing, through which one sucks out the water, but nevertheless I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor do I read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the forms of almagate, so that those who do not know it can see them; and they should be made of pure tin:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And let their heads be of this same delicacy, and their buttocks have three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the flesh from (over) the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Sometimes diverse fleshy growths are born on the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such that have elevated flesh of fox-colored, and such that have soft flesh of good color. In this case of these fleshy growths that is soft, and not elevated, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply the lancet to those growths, and pull them out; then cut what you are able to hold with a sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all of the flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any part remains that cannot be cut, open it with all one of the fine and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if pus forms, or an abscess, treat it as necessary; and if they are harmful abscesses, hurry and cauterize it until the blood stops and all of the flesh is removed, then apply aseptic water or wine to the nose.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the nose does not open, and moisture reaches up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not come out as it should, know that there is flesh growing in the bone above, where the instrument cannot reach; then you must insert a fairly thick linen thread, and have knots at regular intervals of about a finger's width or less; and place the thread in the patient's nose with gentle force, and pull it out while sniffing until it comes out of the nose into the mouth; and many children do this in school, and it is an easy task for those who want to do it; then hold the part that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other part that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and alternate them while being aware of where the knots are on the thread. Continue doing this until you know that the knots have corrupted all of the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment and reinsert it into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment dissolves everything remaining; and then place a piece of wood in the nose for several days until it is healed, and use drying medicines if necessary; and this is the form of the instrument used to cleanse the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, such as a funnel, and the spout similar; and if you wish, make a closed funnel, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle at the top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of flesh from the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often, a disease arises in the head of the nose, which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove all of it, then apply the hot cautery or heated medicine; and if you delay in cutting it until it has grown large, beware if it is hard, with a purple color, and poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut once, great harm can come to the patient; and if the abscess is superficially touched, not with a purple color, and you see that you can remove all of it, then empty the patient's nose and cauterize without fear, and cure the area with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, one must cauterize all the parts of their edge until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a suture and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood and ground incense on top of the powders, and place a piece of plaster of strong ointment or another binding ointment on top, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in abdominal suturing; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To some men, hard abscesses similar to grains of millet appear within the lips, smaller and larger; then it is necessary that you turn the lips, and cut at each nodule, and take them with forceps and cut each part; then apply a poultice of powdered vitriol after the incision until the bleeding stops; and then raise the edges and cure the wound of dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often, a swelling of the flesh occurs on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow out; then put vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if that flesh returns after being cut, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not return after being cauterized. And these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, calluses appear on the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, and green, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; so you must have the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape away the calluses or hardened tissue from the visible teeth until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are removed. And if the decayed matter is removed at the first scraping, that is good; otherwise, resume scraping on the second and third day until everything has been removed. And be aware that teeth require various shapes of instruments to scrape, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used to clean between the teeth have different forms than those used to clean the surface of the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared and with you.[NOTE: I am a language model and my translations are generated by machine learning algorithms, so while I strive for accuracy, there may still be errors or nuances that I miss. Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because one should not do this without good reason; for it is a very important substance up to the point where there is no excuse for extracting it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is ready to have it pulled, you must make sure that you are certain about which tooth is causing pain. Often times, the patient's pain may be felt in a different tooth, and they believe it to be a problematic tooth, leading to the extraction of the good tooth; but even after this, the pain does not subside, because the root of the bad tooth remains. Therefore, when you are certain about which tooth is causing pain, then you must burn a tourniquet around the tooth with a strong electuary to protect the gum from all sides; then pull it with your fingers or fine pliers at the very base until it is loosened well and securely clamped; and have the patient's mouth wide open in front of you, holding them firmly so that they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of those instruments and gently insert it into each side; and wiggle it as you did before. And if the tooth is broken or decayed, then you must fill it with pieces of cloth where the holes are and hold it together delicately with pliers so that it does not break during this process; and it is important to work skillfully around the gum in order to loosen the tooth.[**Emended Translation**]
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And I advise you to be careful not to break it and leave a part of it inside the patient's mouth, as this would cause greater pain than before due to the malice of the root. Also, take care not to act like ignorant surgeons who, in their haste and recklessness, sometimes break the tooth and don't fix what we have described; instead, they bring about great sickness because of the roots that remain or the broken piece, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine or vinegar and salt; if bleeding occurs (which often happens), then fill it with powdered vitriol; and if this doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should be long and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick shanks so that they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of good iron, and serrated to hold (the tooth).
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulling (the tooth), one must put cotton soaked in butter on the wound for one or two days until the area is numbed, then apply tongs called «algefri», which have the appearance of a bird’s beak; and they should be made inside like a file, and this is the shape:
