Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding in order to hold the bone so that it does not slip out, but can rather hold and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rottenness in the bone and it is small, one removes all of it with this tool:[In modern English]
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is not erupted after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is protruding along with the tooth, take this instrument, of which the shape is similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And hold the file carefully and gently in your hands for several days due to the tooth's hardness, so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that the tooth can be filed down, file it with a thin file like this one, of which the shape is as follows:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is similar to the files used for making needles; and file the tooth carefully and gently in your hands several times a day, so that it does not move until it heals; then use a plane rasp at the end, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you should file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue nor distort speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth loosen.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth loosen in front, either from a blow or from falling, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the chips between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more than one, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering it up to the point where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand till it doesn't move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the chips with pincers and assemble them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, so that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it tightened as long as it can bear, and if it comes loose, or the wire breaks, then constrict it again with another wire; if it remains in place, it will serve for its entire time, and this is the method of aligning two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place immediately, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled meddle with it; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the gap where the defect is, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cut the tongue's ligament
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes there is a ligament beneath the tongue that is natural at birth or occurs due to an accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the sick person's mouth and hold their head in your hand, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment. And if there is hardness or knots due to hasty healing of a wound, then insert the hook and cut widely that ligament; and be careful that the incision is not too deep due to the artery that is beneath. And when you have done this, apply a swab of rose water and vinegar or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue. And have the patient change it every night so that the ligament does not heal again. And if bleeding occurs, then put vitriol on top of the wound; and if the blood persists, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery which is good for this. Then cure it with other cures until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a fussey color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, throw the "oncine" (a medical tool) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to your work, put vitriol powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift the leu (a bandage or cloth) easily and gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there come inside the throat swellings which are called "godath", and they are properly called the "two almonds". And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is abscesses of hard consistency and of dark color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, then do not touch it at all with iron, for fear of bloodletting; but leave it until it matures, and then you will open it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of pale color and fine roots, then have the instrument ready to cover (it), but first look to see if the abscess has calmed down and is peaceful. Then make the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and open his mouth and take the sergeant between your hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, like this; and it should be of silver or fine brass as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	and you press the tongue down with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the "oncine" (a medical tool) and insert it in the almond (swelling), and pull it out as much as you can; and pull some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, like this; which resembles a pair of forceps; and yet the cheeks are curved, one towards the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then take pliers, of which this is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision rinse the patient's mouth with warm water, and vinegar, and salt, and if there is bleeding, rinse the patient's mouth with water or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then heal it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses grow in the throat besides the two almonds, so cut them then as you would the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had completely closed her throat, so the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have died if she had remained like this for one or two days. And the abscess was so swollen that it had pushed out two pieces through the two nostrils. I therefore acted quickly and inserted a probe into one of them, then pulled it out and extracted a large quantity of pus; then I put another piece in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and so the blocked passage in the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess increased again and filled the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; then I drained it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it ceased to grow; and I left that place, not knowing what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is thin, then it should be lanced; and the one that is rounded assembled and not long; and it is blood-shot or of a fawn color or black, then it should be avoided to incise it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a trick with cauterization without fear. And the manner of cautery is sharp and pointed. And it is that the patient puts their head in your lap, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and apply live steam, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and use the movement of this instrument, of which this is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a thread placed on the head where the medicine is applied, such as the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and muscular movement carry the medicine from their mouth into the eye, so that it does not go down the throat and make them vomit; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, until you see it absorbed and the irritation of the medicine has calmed down; and if you see any excess, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with the cotton into the corner of the eye, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this frequently until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall out after three or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery of the medicine, do so, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and vervain and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put it on a fire, and bring to a boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong clay, and have an instrument like a spoon in the middle of the pot:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the eyes be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye becomes dead; then start again frequently, until the eye dries up, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and never do it except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to overwhelm the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether healthy.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often one encounters a bone or fish spine, or some other object stuck in the throat; then you must pull out what you can see, and press the patient's tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what is not visible and has lodged itself in the throat, you must make the patient vomit when the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the airborne object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out as we have said, take an instrument made of plastic in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it may enter more easily into the throat, and keep the head raised; and make sure not to touch the epiglottis, so as not to cause choking or push the bone in further; and it is better if the patient inserts the instrument themselves, so they can feel where the airborne object is; then insert it downward, or pull it out completely with the entire instrument until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat vein
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes the veins are treated, as I have said in the division, with medical cures; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after you press their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the vein, then pull it with a tiny hook, or with fine tongs that are suitable for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a hollow needle and put it in the sick person's throat, then put the movement of the needle .1. hot iron, and do this often. And if the patient becomes hoarse all day, then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in with swallowed, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it falls.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a cloth pierced in the middle, and let the hole of the instrument be in this opening; then put your fumigation in it, and the patient puts the end of the tube in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but reaches the vein; and the vein will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the vein, it is when one can see it similar to curved tongs in order to enter easily into the throat; and have the shape of a surgeon's beak, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many similarities of abscess are, according to what the remembrance brings afterward of one and the other in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its likeness itself, and those that hold moisture. And the second way is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the base, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different from those that come in joints, and each one has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its development; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their development, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb. Or the abscess is near the main member, and if you delay the piercing until it is matured, it will harm the main member; or it is near the base, so one must pierce it when it is dead; and one should never pierce a grown abscess without digestion being completed, except for those that are near the base, which may rot inside and elongate, causing fistula; and cannot be healed in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its development, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the lowest part of the abscess, and where it is most prominent; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and tendons and arteries, and all places where there is no crease.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And in those that crease, according to the member. And when the abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better to leave the incision until it is confirmed by digestion being completed, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body's matter will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to the need of the member. And it is necessary to make small incisions in small abscesses, and small holes; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses that require cutting out the core and covering; when it has become as one cloth, and is dead, then you must do as with boils: and there are such that are cut in three angles, and such that are cut like a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses of glands; and there are such that a round incision is made, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who have no visible abscesses, such as a mild subcutaneous one, should be fully lanced; and when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, you should not pull out all the pus in that hour, but instead remove some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and remove something more; do this multiple times, increasing the amount each time, until all the pus is removed; do the same even if the patient is of weak constitution, such as women, young children, old or decrepit men. For the spirit may suddenly jump when the pus is released, causing the patient to die unexpectedly. Therefore, proceed with great caution in this matter, and once you have lanced your abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a clean cut, apply bandages made of linen or old cotton; but if it is large abscesses with many holes, insert a tent into each one so that they press against each other; and if you have cut off part of the skin and pulled it back, you should fill it with old linen rags or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, apply cold and easily absorbable water, and wet a cloth, placing it on the bleeding site multiple times. If the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, using the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, you should place tents and damp cloths soaked in warm oil and vinegar on top; and if it is summer, and the location is fleshy, you should put damp cloths soaked in water and cold oil, or warm vinegar and oil for a whole day as we have said; then loosen the abscess, clean and dress it as required until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is what should be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	"des soros" is likely a misspelling or variant spelling of "des sors," which means "of lots" or "of chances." However, based on the context provided, I believe that the intended word was actually "apostemes," as it is a term commonly used in medical texts to refer to abscesses.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where small abscesses of the head come, and they are of two kinds, as the joints of a chicken, and there are many similar ones. Some are fatty and such where there is moisture, like poultices; and some are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery does not oppose it. And the task of cutting is that you try every single instrument called "entromissoire," from which the form comes as follows, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, so you pierce above the long [one]. And when the moisture is emptied, so skin it without leaving any of the skin that contains that moisture, for it returns again when you leave anything; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will wash it. And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that nothing remains overnight; then cure the wound with a suitable ointment, until it is healed. And if the abscess has a thick fat, so cut it along the long [one]; and throw your leeches there, and skin it all around, and put all your effort into drawing out the cyst that lies there; and if the artery opposes you, so do what I told you after. And similarly do for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And cutting into the hard and moist abscess is easier, for they contain little blood. And some of these abscesses on the head or where there is no moisture, and this was one of the abscesses that I cut on an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as a hard, rough and white stone, and could not break it; and if anyone had struck it, they would have made as much of a wound as from a stone. In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those that come on children's heads and at the roots of the ears, let the incision be always in the lowest dependent place, so that pus can easily exit; and cure them as is necessary.
des scrophules	"Des scrophules" is a term that refers to a type of abscess or swelling, usually found in the neck or jaw area. Scrofula is a form of tuberculosis that affects the lymph nodes and is characterized by the formation of painful, hard lumps under the skin. The term "scrofula" comes from the Latin word "scrofa," which means "female pig," likely because the swollen lymph nodes resemble the appearance of a pig's neck glands. In medieval medical texts like the one you provided, scrophula was often treated through various surgical procedures and the use of ointments or other topical treatments.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	"Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre." This passage describes how scrophula often appears on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin area. It also notes that they can appear elsewhere on the body and can be large and clustered together.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop bleeding, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skill if there remain any small scrofulous lumps, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulous lump, it is not at all appropriate to cut that scrofulous lump in its root, but tie it with a double strong thread, and let it fall without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scrofulous lump, it is necessary to bring the two lips of the wound together and sew them now, since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofulous lump. It is necessary to focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said. As for the scrofulous lumps that hold excess matter, pierce where it appears necrotic; and pierce it in the same way as the one described before, by letting it drain, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the necrosis; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a healing ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	The term "de squinance" in Old French can have different meanings depending on the context. It could refer to sciatica, which is a type of pain that affects the back, hip, and outer side of the leg due to compression or irritation of the sciatic nerve. It can also refer to any kind of sharp or chronic pain in the side, similar to what we call rib pain today. Without more context, it's difficult to provide a precise translation.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the operation of the throat, but I have never seen anyone in our land who performed it, and this is the writing of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	To those who have squinting, it is necessary that the slit of the throat called "epiglottis" be cleared; and this is not done with ease, because all the veins and the windpipe of the patient are swollen in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the windpipe channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid suffocation which results from constriction.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to incise the epiglottis, it is necessary that we make the incision under three or four circles or a small cut across, between the two circles or according to the length of the slit of the syphilis, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these places are suitable for the incision of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long and narrow.[ST1]
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat to its full extent, then split the windpipe until it reaches the windpipe; and release the vessels of blood, if you see any such thing, and then cut the syringe, as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the windpipe that jumps out at the opening where it is broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed where there is doubt of strangulation, bring together the two lips of the windpipe wound, and sew it all the way up to the cartilage; then administer medicines that promote tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that this should not be done until the throat is completely choked up and the patient is judged to be dead and there is absence of breathing.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and they breathe through the wound, and thus they are kept from dying.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And therefore the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and this occurs in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they instructed to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took a knife and plunged it into her throat, cutting some of the tendons in the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to cure it, and found it as if dead.

I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and knew well that it had not received medical attention or been properly treated except for the throat, and the breath was coming out through the wound.

por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	therefore I say that in cutting the epiglottis, one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in the color of a lentil, and it is common in women;

des nous	of the nails
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many types of nails, of which I will describe all the varieties;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and now I must explain the difference that exists between a nail (nout) and an ulcer (issue).

I say that a dislocation is heat and fever-holding, as long as the boiling (inflammation?) has not passed, and the corruption is complete; then the fever abates and the heat subsides.

Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the manner of inquiry for abscesses of the new injury is that you take the moistest place that you find in the abscess and turn your hand this way and that, so that you know that the instrument has penetrated to the core, according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then pull out the [surgical] instrument, and take care that it doesn't leap out (of the wound).
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture collects in a swelling, let it have whatever color it may, then lance it as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the insertion of the surgical instrument, moisture does not come out, know that it is fatty. Then lance it in a cross shape and use forceps to take hold of it, gently skin it from all sides, and pull the cyst carefully with the surrounding flesh so that you can extract it whole.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot pull it out whole, then remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.[Translate]
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if anything remains, the disease will return many times;[Translate]
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if some of it remains and the blood bothers you, apply corrosive powders to the wound, bind the wound, place warm, soothing poultices on it, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the wound is large, cut the two edges of the wound and treat it with remedies that clean out rotting flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein cutting is contrary to you or against another, hurry and apply a vitriol paste, and let it sit for two or three days until the wound festers, allowing the boiling of the blood to subside; then return to covering what remains of the new wound.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Behold the forms of the intromittent instruments, which are of three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and these also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses or fistulas.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are like the needles with which we sew surplices, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are more valuable, and they are better tested for use with black plumb line to encircle the abscesses of fistula;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	and there are three types: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the trocars are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are trocars that have two holes of three types as well;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and there are trocars that have three holes, and they are also of three types; and there are trocars that have two holes, and others with only one hole, and all of them are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The tips of these (trocars) are sharpened, and some only cut on one side so that they dissect the flesh without cutting the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these instruments, the needles are attached to handles, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses;

et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to cure them, must proceed according to the form of this line b to .g.

des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits can be of two types: hard scrofulous ones or those that contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Then those who contain moisture should have their hair cut in this manner, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton and apply a dressing suitable for healing until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofulous sores, open it as we have said for scrofulous sores, and if the wound becomes pus-filled again, apply a hot iron as we have said before.[ ](data:image/gif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAIAAAAAAAP///yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7)
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When an artery is ruptured and the skin over it becomes attached, it often results in abscesses, and similarly, swelling and abscess occur with a vein.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and one knows it thus when it is because of the artery, so is the abscess long and deep;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your hands, it feels like a swelling; and when it is because of the vein, it is bluish in appearance.
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is foolish to cover this abscess, even when it is under the fingernails and toenails, or on the neck and in many other places, for they can be quite large.[Reference(s):
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	Therefore, one must avoid the iron cure, and likewise for those at the head, and in the case of swelling of the artery, make an incision through the skin.[Reference(s):
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then make the incision with probes, and carefully separate the artery from its sheaths until it is fully exposed.[Reference(s):
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle underneath it, and make it pierce through to the other side, and restrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then prick the place that is between the two ligatures with a pointed instrument until blood comes out, and the abscess will be released.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then manage the treatment until the wound heals, until the ligature falls off.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with appropriate ointment until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	And if the abscess is due to an incision of a vein, then you should apply a dye to your hand that you can reach from the abscess to all the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the place that you are holding with your hand, and make it pierce, and have one double thread, so that you draw it from the other side;
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then lay the abscess, as I have told you, with one end of one of the two parts of the thread at the two ends of the incision;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	and if you fear that the thread might come out, then insert another needle at one end of the thread under the entire abscess up to the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads tight in four places;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the pus comes out, then cut away the excess of the incision and leave what is attached;[--------------------------------------------------](https://fr.glosbe.com/fr/en/cut)
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then put a cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then provide care with bandages and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as an abscess can develop in an artery or a vein, so too can an abscess develop in nerves when they are cut or through excessive exertion and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this occurs more frequently in the shoulders and hands, and in all places where there are joints, and these are severe abscesses, and their color resembles the color of flesh, and they can be in various forms without pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	And when it is strongly constricted, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but beneath the chest.[2](https://t.me/DeeplLearnerBot?text=And+when+it+is+strongly+constricted%2C+the+patient+feels+pain%2C+and+it+is+not+deep+in+the+body%2C+but+beneath+the+chest.%0A)
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it can move in all directions without going forwards or backwards, upwards or downwards, and if it is in the joints, it should not be covered with iron, because that may cause constriction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and he who is at the head or forehead, makes the skin (or flesh) incised with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut into its root;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, then suspend it with a string, and flay (peel) it, then remove it (the pus) and bring the wound together with stitches, and treat it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	large, hanging abscesses
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes there are in the belly and not elsewhere teats, and it is a disease that is called "fungi" because of its appearance, and it has fine roots and large heads; and they can be small or very large.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	And I saw one man who had two in his belly that were more similar to mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were overgrown, and moisture was continually running out of them.

З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I weighed them and found that one weighed 18 ounces, and the other 6 ounces, and the operation in the incision consists of looking to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and has fine roots;
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	and then hold it (the limb) in place, and do not cease to hold the piece of plastic (or something similar) in place until it cuts through the tendon, and this should be done without much difficulty; and if the roots are thick, there is a risk of also cutting through the belly, but you can still manage to cut only halfway.
