Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an abscess that has worsened, and I will discuss the treatment of the chancre later in the text.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil bursts open.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of a swelling comes from a cautery of a wound or split of a syfic, and is above the belly and in the groin area, as it happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is mentioned, or from wind;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is from a rupture of the syfic and the exit of the intestine, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and open with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with one's fingers, it becomes firm and then returns, and perhaps it becomes hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and after heavy work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	And if it is due to moisture, then it is a light thing and can easily be felt when pressed with the hand, and does not constrain; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess is large and hard, and becomes fixed according to a certain quantity;
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to flatulence, it is easy to touch, and the procedure is such that you should look if the appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	Then you should leave the treatment. Because there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or a boil, then you should instruct the patient to expose their throat and lie completely flat, and then tie a bandage around the swelling.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	...and then command them to lie still with their head in your hands.
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	...then walk around the area that you have designated for the entire duration of the treatment,
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then extend the middle of the abscess above with a large hook;
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then bind it around with a strong thread or a cord of sturdy silk, tightly, and leave enough loose end of the thread;
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then make an incision in the middle of the abscess which is extended over the thread, and insert your index finger, and search for the intestines;
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you find it caught in the thread, then untie it, and place the intestine back into the abdomen;
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find pus, then take hold of it with the hook, and cut off the excess;
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein resists you, then go around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and put two threads through them, and put the two needles across what you have done in a cross pattern that you made to pierce;
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then constrict the abscess in four stages on the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the area as long as it rots, and let the pus drain by itself;
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	or cut it when it becomes fine and rotten, then treat what needs to be treated, and drain the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as needed, and close the incision.
dou chancre	of the chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have stated in the division the similarities of chancre and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and requires great caution in its treatment, and the ancients said that when chancres are in a place where they can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it first begins; and when it is large and old, one must not approach it at all, for I have never cured anyone of it; nor has anyone cured it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient of black bile once; then make them bleed if they have clear signs of fullness; then prepare the patient for the procedure; then cast your leeches onto the chancre and remove all hair from around it without leaving any behind; and let the blood flow freely, and clean the area thoroughly with your hand or some other object; and if the bleeding is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until the bleeding stops; then cure the wound until it heals.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look whether the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as pleurisy and loosening of the bowels and similar things; if there is doubt, do not touch it with iron; but if you see the patient to be of strong virtue, and they have no other illness but dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed in this way:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lay the patient upright on your hands, and have the assistant press the abdomen by pushing the water to the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula according to this form: And let it be sharpened in two parts to a point, but yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot wound;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	then look if the dropsy has extended towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the bladder three fingers deep and straight below the navel; and if it is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the bladder three fingers; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is necessary that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the waste does not run to this weak place.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	then pierce all the way through the skin with your instrument and insert it, and lift your hand with the spatula in between the skin and bladder to the width of a finger; then pierce the bladder until the spatula reaches the place of the water, which is the location of the incision; then drain the water out and insert this instrument with this shape: And it is similar to a thin silver cane, made of brass or light iron, and has one small hole on the underside; and on the side there are three holes; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the incision is shaped like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that writers make the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	upon the head is the Adam's apple, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it then subsides onto the tool; empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than is appropriate at that hour, perhaps the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he will fall unconscious, or he will approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the amount of its strength, and according to what the dispositions of the patient's strength indicate, and his pulses; then pull the tool and hold the water, which is now stopped by the kidney that plugs the opening above the bladder, which I mentioned, that you pierce in this manner; then resume the tool the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw a small amount of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	do this for several days and be careful not to empty too much, leaving only a small amount of water. And if you are uncertain about the patient, and leave too much water, then cure them with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and let him drink; and cure them with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of water, as I mentioned before.
de l’estopement de la verge	This text appears to be incomplete and does not make sense on its own. It seems to refer to "l'estopement de la verge," which translates to "the stoppage of the penis" in English. However, this phrase does not fit into the context provided by the previous sentences.
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Sometimes a child is born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small or not in its proper place. In such cases, it is necessary to make a tiny incision of one spatulam (a unit of measurement) with a very fine awl following this form: then insert a fine plug of linen cloth and bind and keep it in place for three or four days. When the child needs to urinate, remove the plug and allow urination, then replace the plug. It may happen that there is no need to replace the plug, since the urine coming out will not close the opening.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	The one whose opening is small can be treated with a linen plug as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, causing them to be unable to urinate until they lift their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the opening, and this is a bad condition.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the procedure is as follows: have the patient lie down on their back, then stretch out the head of the penis and hold it so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; take care to avoid excessive bleeding which can occur, and if it does, stop the bleeding with a styptic and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	pustules on the penis.
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these ulcers appear on the penis, and it is a hideous appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and benign ones; so you should take them with a subtle probe, and cut and clean all (of it), then put a cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with defvinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and discharge, then you should apply cautery to it. Once you have cut it out, and if the ulcer is in the middle of the penis, and has a part inside the skin and a part outside, then you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is healed, then cure the one on the outside. Because when you cure them together, the tip of the penis is not secure and can be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come to the penis and the groin; so you must cut away all that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster made of honey and flour from the bark of pomegranates and vinegar, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And if bleeding occurs, then apply lunar cautery in the following manner: The cautery helps with two conditions together: namely, bleeding and corruption; and if the ulcer of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then you should insert a reed of plumbers' wax into the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin on the head of the penis (that has not been circumcised) becomes dry due to wounds or abscesses, then you must scrape it with a small instrument until the foreskin is loosened, and the tip of the penis is freed from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if this is difficult to do, then you should scrape it with a small spatula on the head of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate it between two, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water, so that it does not become dry again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the same as loosening a continuation like other wounds; yet when we perform this work of our own volition, and particularly on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not practice circumcision on their children, as they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen that the majority of masters and healers who performed circumcision did so with a lancet around one day old, and sometimes with forceps and a scalpel; the foreskin is avoided because there are two layers to it, and by chance, the one above may be cut while leaving the one below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or sometimes the foreskin is left and causes double pain, and at the circumcision done around a day old, the cleansing of the penis's tip is not guaranteed; and in the cleaning of the nail, by chance the iron may slip, and they ruin the work, and many times it happens that it doesn't require cleaning, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the suturing that is done with forceps on the entire length of the wound, I have found the strength of the experiment to be good, for the forceps cut precisely both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, you cut evenly in a single steady motion; but let the thread be tightly wrapped around the skin; and the first task is to make the child think, if they pay attention, that you are only tying the thread around the member, and then cheer them up in every way that you can;
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then hold the member straight between your hands and place the forceps either in your hands or beneath your feet so that the child cannot see them or any of the instruments; then place your hand on the member and blow and draw it up until the head of the member is exposed; then clean it well of any collected filth, then tie a double thread signet around the base, then tie another knot below; and hold it with two fingers at the second knot between the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two knots; then quickly lift the foreskin up and draw back the head of the member.
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Let the blood flow a little, for this is beneficial; then apply powder and on top of that place a gauze strip soaked in egg white mixed with rosewater, combined with good and fresh red oil, and leave it on until the next day and continue to care for it until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The procedure for purging is as follows: let the two ends (of the instrument) be even and sharp, and let them be of equal length as the handle.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in purging is when the heart exits through the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the place forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers and cut it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if it (the abscess) exceeds for three days, and the part beneath the groin is swollen, then let it be until the abscess has calmed down; and carefully remove the scab; cut it as you can move it, and be careful not to damage the part of the groin, it will not harm anything.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat then the wound with dry powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut too deeply into the heart and it goes above, it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	about retaining urine

Have the patient sit on a seat and massage their bladder and penis with moist olive oil and warm water;[In this medieval medical treatise, the method for relieving urinary retention involves using a silver syringe with a thread attached to wool or cotton at the tip. The excess wool is trimmed, and the syringe is coated in a mixture of oil, butter, and egg yolk. The patient is then instructed to sit on a seat, and their bladder and penis are massaged with moist olive oil and warm water. If urination does not occur, it is suggested that the stone may be located higher up in the bladder or urethra, causing further discomfort for the patient.]
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	then gently insert the syringe into the member, until it reaches the base of the member, then bend the member upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel it reach the empty place, and this is not done in any other order except that the conduit through which it passes may be twisted; then stretch the string along the entire length of the woolen cloth, and the urine will follow the cloth, then pull it out, and let the urine flow.
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	and repeat the process of inserting the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient will be relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder diseases.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you wish to distill water and medicines into it, then make sure all the instruments used are clean, especially the one called "clepsedre", and this is its form:

et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.
