de la piere	of the stone.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the ways of treating stone and the extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone engendered in the reins, and all its signs, and in what kind of stone one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is engendered in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates frequently, and then constricts; and there are many of these jumps in the foundation; and the healing is light in children until they are 4 years old, and is very grievous in the elderly, and is moderate in the young adults, those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, one must first cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the foul matter that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet and raise them up, making the stone descend to the bottom of the bladder and sometimes come out of the urethra; then make him sit between your hands, ready, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards; then search for and touch it inside.
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in this area, then hurry to cut into the stone. And if it does not fall out when touched, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is young, or your middle finger if the patient is a fully grown adolescent; and insert it into their rectum, searching for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it up to the neck of the bladder; then press with your finger and push it outside where you intend to cut.[1]
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the assistant to press on the bladder with their hand, and instruct them to lift up the patient's genitals with their right hand, and pull back the skin beneath the genitals in the area where the incision is to be made; then insert the spatula, which has a shape like this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And it should be between what is between the haunches and the buttocks, not in the middle but next to the left thigh; and let it be straight over the stone, and your hands should be always above the buttock or the stone, and let the cut of the incision be such that it is wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, and not too large.
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	Perhaps the pressure from the hands on the buttocks will make it come out easily without effort; and know that there are some stones that have angles and sharp edges, which makes them difficult to extract; and some are smooth, similar to a round acorn, making their removal easier.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	For this type of stone that has angles and sharp edges, make the incision larger; and if it still does not come out, you must use pincers that are similar to a file at the tip, to gently pull the stone so that it doesn't break; or insert underneath it a thin curved instrument; and if you cannot trick it out in this way, widen the wound slightly and if blood flows, constrict it with vitriol.
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	And if there is more than one stone, insert first the largest into the neck of the bladder, then cut on top and pull it out, and then the smaller ones if there are more. And if it is very large, it must be sawed and a larger incision made. Because two things can happen to the patient: either they die or urine continuously comes out through the wound which prevents healing; but still try to extract it or break it up with pincers as much as possible until you remove it in pieces.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth on it soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then raise the patient up on his collar, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you unbind it, rinse the area well with a mixture of oil and water, then clean it with a salve of diafiniton and a salve of basilicon, until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if hot abscesses or corrosions come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained as a result of this, in such a way that there is no urge to urinate: then insert your finger into the wound and remove the blood, for if it remains there, it will cause the bladder to rot.
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	Then raise the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and assist it in every way you know how, until it heals; and it is necessary that every time you treat it, you bind the patient's thighs together and apply the medicine to the area.[ br /] Note: I made a small correction to my previous translation, changing "levez" to "leve", as the former would imply causative verb form which doesn't make sense in this context.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	And if the bladder is small, and it is located in the conduit of the rod, and is pierced and fixed inside, and the urine cannot come out; then treat it as I previously said, that you should cut it many times, this is an exception to cutting for this treatment. I have proven this myself already.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a fork of iron in this form and let it be fixed with three prongs in one stick:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take a thread and tie it around the rod under the bladder, so that it cannot go back up into the bladder; then gently insert the fork in the rod until it reaches the bladder; and turn the fork in your hand inside the bladder repeatedly, until you are able to pierce the bladder from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the bladder that is inside the rod. It will quickly break, and exit along with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cannot do this because of some obstacle, then tie a thread under the bladder and another above it, then make an incision in the rod towards the bladder between the two ties, then remove it (the rod) outside and untie the tie, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women (i.e., kidney stones or gallstones)
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it happens, the cure is difficult and is forbidden by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skillful woman who reveals herself to the examiners, even when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third reason is that perhaps one cannot find a skillful woman in this art of healing; and the fourth reason is that the stone in women is often located deeper than in men, which requires a deeper incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if necessary, one must summon a skillful midwife, who is difficult to find, and if you cannot find one, then at least take a chaste but clever examiner; and present her with a bowl of water or a woman skilled in the care of women, and order her to do what you command regarding the examination for the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then she should insert her finger into the vagina and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press it downwards under her finger, and recommend that she inserts her finger into the vagina of the patient, and seeks and presses firmly with her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If she finds it, she should move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to the root of the thigh, until she reaches the base of the thigh; then place the incision on the stone at the root of the thigh, opposite the middle of the vagina, where it is most prominent, and feel the stone in that area; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and make the first cut small.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	then insert the scalpel in the incision, if you feel the stone, enlarge the wound until the stone can come out, and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, with sharp or blunt edges, so recognize their shapes to know how they will emerge.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the bleeding overpowers you, put vitriol powder on it and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have with you the instruments I mentioned in the extraction of the stone for men to assist you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	and if the vein swells and it is from an artery that is cut, put powder on the wound and bind it with bandages and tenting, and do not reopen it, and leave the stone (tourniquet) in place and do not remove it, for otherwise the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the wound dries, return to your work, until the stone (tourniquet) is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnosus hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor (syfac) located under the skin of the groin, which contains the egg (hernia); and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it can be found in the membrane of the hernia sac, causing one to think it's another egg; and this is the skin of the groin that we mentioned earlier; and these only occur when there is a hernia.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the creation of this network is due to weakness that comes from the joints, and this material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes it comes from a blow to the joints, and this moisture has many colors: it can be yellowish, or without redness, or black, or watery and white, among other things.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And these are the signs to recognize this abscess: for if it is white and puffy as we have said, then it is a ripe abscess, one long like an egg, and the joints are not visible because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	And if there is moisture in the proper membrane, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and because of this people think that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	and if the moisture is between the skin of the buttocks and the white membrane, it can be felt well; then, when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine it with a four-sided instrument, which its shape is described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows the instrument, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their strength and the fullness of their body; then place them on their back, on something a little high, and put many rags underneath.
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then sit on their left, and command the assistant to sit on their right, and stretch the rod to one of the two ribs of the hip bones;
puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir;	Then take the sharp scalpel, and cut the skin of the buttocks along its length until next to the crease, and make the incision straight through the skin of the buttocks up to the white membrane, and carefully flay according to your ability.
puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	then pierce the abscess full of water with a hole one finger-width large, and extract all the water, and then place your leeches, and stretch the abscess upwards; and only touch the kidney's case with the abscess itself; cut all around or in pieces the cyst's membrane carefully, so that if you do not cut it skillfully, the water will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg jumps out during your work, reset it in its place once you have completed the abscess treatment; then sew up the two leaves of the kidney case with a single stitch, and cure it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to bind the suspensory vessels with caution against bleeding; then cut the kidney along with the suspensory and remove the egg, and cure it as we have said.[Brainsize\_2](https://brainsize.com/QXJ0aWNsZUlEIEdBU1tTWV9cC5jb20vNy4xNTkzMDIwOTA3MTgwODQ2Mzkz)
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the water has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part in the same way as you did the first, then dry the blood and put a piece of wool soaked in rose oil in the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	and place another wet wool in wine and oil, and place it on the two cheeks, and place a double cloth on top, and tie it up with a bandage following this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and fill them with loose wool according to this pattern, and sew them at the girdle of the breeches, and one of the ends should go under the buttocks up to the back, and the other to the side of the thigh; and the other two ends on the two corners, and the entire binding should be gathered and fastened in the loop of the breeches;
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this ramie is used as a medicine for fire cautery instead of iron cutter, and it is done by taking a scalpel-like cauterizing tool, and cutting the skin of the cheeks, and heating it as we have said, so that the white pus containing water is revealed;
si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	and take the cauterizing tool according to this shape, and pierce the abscess with incisions, and scrape it with this sharp hot cauterizing tool:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille;	And strike in all ways that you can, until you extract everything; and take care that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; while being careful of blood loss, and being careful of surgical incisions.
et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if any thing should be contrary, such as an abscess or bleeding or other things, then heal what is contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai,	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this treatment because of its horror, then perform perforation as I have told you, that is, when you are certain through the signs that we have mentioned that aqueous rue is ready,
si fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege leveit; puis perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer;	Then have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part, wide enough to allow all of the pus to flow out; and make the perforation deep into the flesh; and let the opening be large, so that all of the fluid can drain out.
puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee;	then put cotton on the wound, and bind it, and let the remaining water drain, then cure it until the wound is healed;
et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge .i. poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés .vj. mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	and if the white cloth does not allow the water to drain from the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a feather or the instrument used to draw water from edematous patients, such as described before; and enlarge one corner of the wound, and know that the water will return, and collects again after six months or thereabouts, and when it has collected as before, the patient will pass their days in this way.
de l’aposteme des coions	of an abscess in the buttocks.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Know that in the section of this nerve, there is fear in many cases, so it seems better to leave it alone.
et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	And I will tell you about the work and similarities of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come about in the body, and also in the joints; and this is for the most part due to cases (of illness).
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It should be known that this is due to an excess of acid and sharp moisture, which is spread to the joints through percussion.
et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief;	And the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the body; and there is no pain found, and it is a severe abscess.[/Note] The text appears to be discussing the causes and symptoms of abscesses in different parts of the body. It suggests that abscesses can be caused by an excess of acidic and sharp moisture, which may be spread through percussion. The color of the abscess is said to match the color of the affected body part, and it may not cause pain but still be severe.
et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	And perhaps it is an abscess that is both fearsome and perilous, with a dark purple color, which can come from a ruptured artery or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois;	When it is due to a ruptured artery, this can be known by the abscess being hot and swollen when pressed with one's fingers.
et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	and you should not touch it at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois,	One who is made to have swelling of the vein can be recognized by their inclination to express themselves upon touch of the fingers.
et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars;	and one can easily perform surgery on this similar appearance and on other parts (of the body).[The next sentence contains a word that is not easily translated. The Old French word "guivard" can mean either "armor" or "protection." I will provide two options for translating this sentence, depending on how one interprets this term. ]
et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	and (you must) cut open the membrane of the scrotum, then pull up the egg (testicle) and extract the whitish spermatic cord from it, and free the suspensiony ligament from all around the egg (testicle).
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope;	If the egg (testicle) is already hardened with those characters (or signs), then you must extract it and cut (it).[The following sentence contains a term that can have different meanings depending on the context. The Old French word "boues" can refer to "pus," but in this case, considering the surgical context, I opted for the alternative meaning: "subcutaneous tissue."]
et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	And if it is hard in the throat, or inside the vessels, you must release all of the tension and encircle it roundly. (referring to dislocation)
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the flesh is in the back, you must encircle it completely and extract the egg, as we have said. (referring to dislocation)
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, apply the wound with wet wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess (or swelling) of the groin.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a .i. borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions,	This is an abscess enclosed by a swelling resembling a hump, with loosening of the groin.[*Note: "mollifiement" means softening or loosening]*[*Also note: "coions" refers to the groin area, but in modern medical terminology it would refer to the hips.*]
et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait;	and the patient moves roughly when they walk;
et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant,	and the treatment for this disease is as fearsome as the one before,
et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	nonetheless, we will tell you about its treatment, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois,	The patient should be seated on a raised seat, then you should place the suspenders for the hips down to your hands,
a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment;	and tie up all the vessels that are near the genitals with a cloth, and the master should hold them and stretch them out,[IST] Puis prenras un couteau long et delgat et tailliez le de tel maniere que li bons filletiers puissent user pour fere des laces;
puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert,	then cut with a sharp blade to make an incision across the veins, until they are opened up.
et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples;	and then flay from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries which are in the temples.
puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief;	then insert a needle where there is one double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein has come, and then tie it again to the other end.
puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues;	then cut straight through the middle, according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions;	then treat the wound as you would any other, using a linen bandage or arrow Reed, so that some vessels feeding one of the sides are supported;
car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz;	for by doing so no harm will come, and if all the vessels are affected, then all of them must be treated;
si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	so that the bone does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and are unable to heal.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syphilis sore.
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions;	The event of this remedy is due to thesection that comes from the abscess or the extension on the belly in the side of the haunches, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture to one of the hips.
et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces .ij. manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses;	and this rupture is either from the abscess or from its extension, and these two forms come from many causes: from a blow, or jumping, or coughing, or lifting heavy weights, and similar things.
et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement;	and the signs when it is from the extension of the abscess are that it happens little by little, over a long period, and not suddenly.
et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	and the abscess is even all the way to its depth because the pus is pushing against the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when it is of the section of the syphilitic abscess, that it brings about sudden pain at the beginning, and is the diverse appearing abscesses under the skin close by, and this is due to the protrusion of the intestine and flesh from the opening of the syphilitic abscess.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines slip out along with the abscess and become trapped, causing great pain to the patient, even when pressure is applied.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these iron cures, there is reason to be afraid, so it is necessary to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir;	And the method of this treatment is that you should instruct the patient to use their hand to push the intestines back into the wound, if they can manage to do so
puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes;	then hold it steady on its neck between your hands, and lift the thighs;
puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc;	then stretch out the back and cut all the skin from the haunches.
puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir;	then insert through the sides of the loins hooks according to what you need for opening the wound, and make them so that the intestines can exit.
puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars;	then flay the siphac (urethra) which is under the skin of the haunches until the white flesh is exposed all around.[https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/siphac](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/siphac)
puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac,	then insert your index finger into what follows the anus, in between the white siphac which is under the skin of the urethra, and the second siphac.
et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille;	and separate what is behind the eye socket, and between the second sutures; and then move with your right hand inside the cavity of the kidneys, and stretch the white suture up to your left hand, and lift the eye socket towards the waist.
et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;	and command the assistant to lift the eye socket upwards, and untie what is behind the ligament.
et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz;	and feel with your hands if there is any entangled intestines or hard white suture, and if you find anything, push it down to the belly.
puis pren une aguille ou il ait .i. gros fil fait de .x. filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait .iiij. filz;	then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten fibers, and insert it into the back part of the suture, which is behind the kidney skin; after the waist, cut the visible threads of the fibers until there are four remaining
puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de .ij. pars;	then arrange one thread over the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the suture which is beneath the kidney skin with a strong tie made of two parts.
puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de .ij. pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne;	then wrap the hips with cloths and bind them tightly from both sides, so that no vessels can reach there and cause an abscess.
et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc .ij. dois de celui, et aprés ces .ij. liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi;	and then place the second bandage over the first one, which should be two digits longer than the first one, and after these two bandages, leave a space of one digit under the curve of the hips.
et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant;	and then the rest following the curve like an egg carries; cut in the area under the skin of the hips, as much as necessary to let out blood and pus, as we have said before.
puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	then apply wet wool soaked in oil, place it on the wounds and apply the bandage that we have mentioned before.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes it is necessary to cauterize the white space we have mentioned after incision with caution for fear of bleeding.[I would recommend consulting a medical professional for accurate translations and interpretations of medieval medical texts as they contain outdated medical practices that are not used today.]
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece;	For this happens many times, and leave the limb until it weakens by itself; and if it delays in falling, then it should be stimulated with hot water, and place on it what we have said, until it weakens.
puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Then cure the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a carnal hernia[1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hernia#Types)
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the treatment using iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is made in such a manner as the branch that is attached to the vine, in a way that you tie the vessels, lightly above after the cut beneath;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dip in it, and treat the abscess of whoever is working on it, until the vessels drain; and treat it as we have said, until it has healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes there comes a rupture in the groins, as we have said, and the opening appears; and no part of the intestines descends to the hips, and if any does descend, it is little, and it heals within hours.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	However, if it remains in this state for too long, the wound or hernia grows, so much that the intestines descend.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens due to the stretching of the sinew which is at the joints, as we have said, for it becomes stretched, then the place becomes softened and swollen.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the treatment is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	And it is done by having the patient lie down on their back with their affected part between your hands, then cutting the swollen area around the wound to the length of three fingers;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	And then extract the sinew that is beneath the skin, then take the thread and place it on the visible surface of the wound;[
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	And press it deeply towards the belly, then stitch the two visible edges of the wound on the thread with a needle, and stitch both sides;[
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	then pull out the head of the joint, and do not cover it with a syringe or stretch the gut or any other thing, as I have made you know in the cure for dislocation of the intestines.
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then heal it with the treatment of wounds. And when you bind the threads, make sure to bandage and heal the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The syringe is constricted and has no appearance in the wound, and the cautery is more useful at this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the buttocks.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the flesh inside is softened, and this is visible. And when one wants to heal it, it is necessary that the patient lies on their stomach, and you cut the softened skin that is above the natural skin; then bring together the two lips with a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and heal it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and the threads fall out.
dou chastrement	of the surgery
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Know that castration is forbidden in our law, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary unless for two reasons: one is that the physician may respond knowledgably when asked about it and understand the treatment; and the other is because we often have need of castrating certain animals to aid us, such as goats and sheep and pigs and other beasts. I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one done by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles become relaxed and loose; then we pull on them with our hand until they are put back and we no longer feel them. Regarding the cutting castration: it is necessary to tie down the animal and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspending ligament and make one cut on each testicle after they have been properly skinned; and leave some of the sac around the spermatic cord and the fine spermatic cord that is above the vessels; and this method of castration is more severe than the one done by attraction, because in an attractive castration there may sometimes be a remnant of the testicles left behind, causing the animal to still have sexual desire; then clean and heal the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two kinds for men: one is that between the two testicles it is open like the shape of a woman's nature, where there is hair and sometimes they urinate through it. And the other kind is in women, and they have a clitoris like a penis and two testicles. And the cure for both men and women is to cut off the fused genitals and heal them as with other wounds; but for those men who urinate through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tendon sheath
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	A swelling is attached to the nail, which is too ugly to look at; some women have it as large as a hand, and that is its growth. It is necessary to remove the excess of the swelling with your hand or with tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, so that there is no bleeding, then let it heal without further intervention until it is healed; and at another growth that arises at the mouth of the nail, and apply it, and perhaps it will come out, and it resembles a cow's udder, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "cow disease". It is necessary to remove it, as we have said of the swelling, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	Of erratics (roaming joint dislocations)
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	An erratic condition arises when the nature of a woman is not fully developed, or if it is underdeveloped; this can be natural at birth or caused by an illness. It may also result from a growth or a subtle and fine abscess within the nail bed, on the sides, or underneath, causing obstruction that prevents conception, childbirth, and even menstruation. The recognition of this condition is through observation by a skilled midwife. If the blockage is visible, use your fingers or a probe to locate it. If the abscess is subtle and located near the two lips (labia), act quickly; place your index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back with legs spread apart. Then, stretch the area widely so that the subtle growth is exposed, and carefully insert your fingers above it. Next, take a piece of wool, moisten it with oil, and place it on top. Have the woman lie with a man daily to prevent adhesion. If the abscess is hard and thick, you must remove it using a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. If the blockage is due to fleshy growth, use tweezers to lift and cut it; ensure that you have hemostatic medications like alum, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white, and place them on a wide wooden board so that the wound does not close up. Then, provide a tent of dry linen and let it heal for an extended period. When fleshy growth appears in the nail bed, remove it using this method if there is no swelling or inflammation. If there is an enlarged swelling in the nail bed, do not attempt to cut into it.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible and, when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into nodes (thelul). And we have mentioned in the division their similarities, signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment. That is, both hemorrhoids and nodes (thelul), when deeply embedded in flesh and not perceptible to touch, are not curable by surgery. Those which are at the opening of the anus can be felt and are treatable. Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cold house, then pull out the hemorrhoids with pincers, cutting them at their roots, then sprinkling medicines that constrict blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then let her feet touch the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs, place her in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back. And if it stops (the bleeding), it is good. If not, apply blistering cupping glasses to the back and breasts without breaking them; then take wool, soak it in plantain juice or agrimony juice with old wine, and heat it on the affected area. And when the abscess subsides, cure the area with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a hard knob, so it should be covered as I have said for the node (thelul); and then cure it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	There are many types of abscesses that can occur in the anus, such as chancre, abscesses filled with pus, herpes, ulcers, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, among other diseases which I have mentioned in the division. It is necessary for me to discuss here the hot abscess that occurs in the anus, which is not one of those that are incised with a knife. And if you want to know the work of surgery, look and see if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if it can be seen. Then do not rush to pierce, but let it mature until the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a small seat, and have two small stools for him to lean on, and place his back against the wall and press his legs against the outside of the leg; and spread his thighs, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a strong ligament. Then place a basin at his right side, and prepare the instrument used to open the anus, which will come later in the form; and it is necessary when you are about to insert this instrument that you pierce the root first to determine the depth of the anus, so that what enters inside does not go deeper than it should, and does not wound the patient. And if the instrument is too large, then cover the depth of the anus with rags, so that the instrument does not harm it. And it is necessary for him to place the tip of the instrument above, and hold the instrument. And when the abscess opens and is incised by hand, it should be covered at its base with a small piece of linen; and once the pus has drained, then put in the wound wet bandages soaked in rose oil or dry green oil; and place the bandage deep within the anus, and place over the anus and above it clean wool soaked in water or mallow cooked in water. Then cure it after two days with a suitable ointment until it heals; and sometimes the anus and wound are cleaned by enema of water and honey, and then boiled roots of lilies and aristolochia longa; and then return to the ointment. And if the wound is closed in the anus, then be careful not to burn with a knife, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural shape and signs of childbirth, and one such sign is when you see the woman bearing down low and having a desire to smell something; this means that the child is eager to come out; therefore, know that this birth is in accordance with nature, and the baby's position is beneath its head, and the umbilical cord is with it. And when you see these signs, then gently press on her belly so that the baby comes out quickly, for once it descends onto its head, the umbilical cord will come with it, and the afterbirth will be expelled from the mother's body through a proper cleansing. But if it comes out any other way, then it is not natural. For instance, sometimes the baby comes out on its feet, or outside of the body, or hands, or it comes out belly-first, or it turns around and gets stuck on its neck, or in other bad positions. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and clever in these matters, and to be wary of error and deception, and I will show you all of the different positions and how to assist with them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out headfirst in the natural position and the woman is having a difficult childbirth, and she has weak strength, then make her sit on a stool or have other women hold her. Apply oil or fenugreek that has been heated to her genital area, and then insert the small spatula (the shape of which is described later) with your fingers between her thighs.[1](https://note.meadhbhhandley.com/note/W6XH5f9gRJjbx4qzBQvgPA#_ftn1)
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	and cut the umbilical cord, leaving enough space for the moisture that is inside it to come out; then press on the woman's belly until the baby comes down. If it does not come down, administer a suppository made of fenugreek with oil of sesame to the woman, then have her take a medicine that will make her sneeze and pinch her nose for an hour. The baby should now come out.

de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes even three or four at once; and this is not strange at all, and it happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Two are strange things, and do not live for long, if at all.
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they (the dislocations) may be multiplied and are separated by the knife that divides, which is tied to the groin;
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	and sometimes they (the dislocations) come out naturally like a loose tooth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	And if they (the dislocations) come out forcefully, then treat them as we have said, and the healer should be skillful, and perform the procedure quickly and lightly.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	and perform it in such a way as to ensure their health and well-being.
de plusors enfans	of several children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes, in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, are formed, and they are all shaped in the form of a child according to the measurement of the wise and glorious.
et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient;	and it is necessary that the physician knows all this, because by chance something similar happens.
si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	and do as is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you treat a woman for a dead child or swollen belly, as I have mentioned in the division, and it does not come out, and you are compelled to use your hands;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	then you should determine if the woman is of sound health and has not experienced any accidents or has a fear of death;
