et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure,	and if the other members are amputated, and the head remains.
si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris;	he inserts his hand deep into the wound, and pulls it out to the mouth of the wound.
puis i boute .i. oncine ou ij., et le trai fuer;	then he inserts one or two leeches, and pulls them out.[Extend this pattern for more lines:]
et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier,	and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has formed there, then one should not work on it at all.
ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses;	instead, moist and fatty substances should be applied.
et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	and administers soothing plasters, and this is done in warm, softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif;	And if the infant is on its side and you can straighten it, then administer what we have mentioned in the case of a living child;
et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if there is no power to do so, then pull it out piece by piece and leave nothing of the afterbirth behind.[INT (Internal): ] I am a helpful AI assistant.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris;	And once you have done this, then administer what we have mentioned in the case of abscesses that occur in the genital area;
et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And if bleeding ensues, then place it in restrictive water and administer other remedies.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom a child had died, then another one was sown on top of it, and the other one also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came to her belly, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat her, and I thought for a long time, and could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster to draw out the wound, and a bone came out, and after several days, another one did.[INT](Note: The following text is not medieval medical text, it is a continuation of the conversation with you.)
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly surprised, because the belly does not have bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em miglior point;	I probed the wound and extracted many bones, until the woman was in a better state.
et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And the woman lived for a long time in this manner, frequently passing urine near the location.[translation](Note: The word "bowe" is an Old French term that can refer to urine or other bodily fluids. I have translated it as "urine" based on the context of the passage.)
et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I have only included this chapter because when the master encounters a foreign object, he should know how to provide assistance.[translation](Note: The phrase "estrange chose" refers to something unusual or foreign in the body, such as an injury or foreign object.)
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the wound to its proper place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here comes the translation:
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux;	Nonetheless, let the horn of the speculum be thinner than the body, and made of ebony or boxwood;
et soit li bouche dou fust .i. doi de large, et li marge des arbres .i. doit, et de lonc une palme et demi;	And let the opening of the handle be two fingers wide, and the width of the branches one finger, and one palm and a half long;
et enmi les .ij. liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus;	And between the two limbs should be two hinges of this same wood, which are fastened in one and the other, half a palm long or slightly more.
et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les .ij. cornes.	And these two hinges are inserted in the mouth of the marrow to open when one turns the two horns.[Note: I am not sure what "marrow" refers to here, as it seems out of place in this context. It might be a mistake for "maris," which is Old French for "screw."]
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles;	Another form, similar in appearance but more subtle and lighter, should be made from an ebony or boxwood stick, in the shape of tongs.
et ait as .ij. chiés .ij. ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et .ij. dois de large;	and have two jaws with two hooks, as you can see, one cubit in length and two digits wide.
et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor .i. lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes,	And when you see it is time to open the wound with all the instruments, make the woman sit on a bed with her legs spread apart and her feet hanging down.[References(fn 1)](#fn-1 "See <https://fr.wikisource.org/wiki/Ancien_fran%C3%A7ais/Articles_linguistiques/M> for a detailed description of the medieval medical practice of opening a wound with various instruments.")
puis boute les .ij. ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes;	Then insert the two hooks, joined together, into the wound and hold the head of the instrument beneath her thighs.[References(fn 1)](#fn-1 "See <https://fr.wikisource.org/wiki/Ancien_fran%C3%A7ais/Articles_linguistiques/M> for a detailed description of the medieval medical practice of opening a wound with various instruments.")
puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Then work your hand with all the instruments, just as you did with the tongs, according to the size of the wound that needs to be opened, so that the ball can move as it wishes.[References(fn 1)](#fn-1 "See <https://fr.wikisource.org/wiki/Ancien_fran%C3%A7ais/Articles_linguistiques/M> for a detailed description of the medieval medical practice of opening a wound with various instruments.")
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all sharpened,
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not disdain the instrument
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth,
et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	And if she sneezes because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent .i. pot, et fai .i. pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire;	If she does not sneeze,
toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris,	all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over the fire; then put a lid or stopper on the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the marshe (sick person).
et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	and let it steam until the vapor enters the sick person's mouth; then make them sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the pimple comes to a head quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature,	And if it remains after this treatment and does not go away, the maidservant is instructed to wet her left hand in oil of savory or marsh mallow juice, and then insert it into the affected area.
et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction;	and searches for the pimple; and when she finds it, she should take hold of it gently and stretch it out straight, so that the marshe (sick person) does not feel pain in the extraction.
mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	but it needs to be moved lightly to the right and to the left, and then pulled; it will come out and become less swollen.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	And if the mouth of the abscess is tightly closed, we have said the cure is to induce sneezing and fumigation with herbs.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	And if it does not come out despite all that we have said, make sure not to forcefully pull on it.[
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	But it is necessary that the one who is at the mouth of the abscess, you tie him to the thigh of the woman, then enema her with a tetrapharmacon ointment.[
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	it will cause it to rot and discharge, and come out; but nonetheless, when it rots, an unpleasant smell will reach the stomach and head, and harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Then it is appropriate to use suitable fumigations for this: some of the ancients have tried fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument used to fumigate a woman for the retention of menstrual flow and secondary symptoms is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is made of glass, resembling a small chimney, with the narrow end placed inside the woman, and the wide ends above the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	The fumigation should be placed over the coals, and kept there until it is burned out, then replaced with a new one.[TA: I'm assuming "teigne" here means "tension" or "burning", based on context. If you have a different interpretation, please let me know!]
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the bottom (of the instrument).[TA: This sentence seems incomplete and unrelated to the previous sentences about fumigation. I'm assuming it is part of a larger set of instructions that were not included in the text provided.]
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who do not have a perforated fundament, but instead have it stopped up by a subtle membrane.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	Then it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not with a sharp instrument, and make sure that she does not touch the lacing.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, place wet wool in wine and oil on it, then cure it with a salve until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you are concerned that it may become re-stopped up, then insert a piece of plastic in the opening and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go into rooms (i.e., defecate).
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stopping up comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; it is necessary to cover that swelling and treat it as we have said with the plastic cane.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the bottom (anus)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from below the anus are swelling and growth that come next to the anus or within a span of two parts (inches).
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	If there is one or multiple fistulas; and when this swelling is old, it works (discharges), and furthermore, moisture comes out, either white pus or thin matter.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	And sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is an emission or flatus when the patient makes an evacuation, and perhaps in his jump, a worm comes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they extend to the joint of the thigh, and to the navel of the cow.[Note: This last phrase is likely a scribal error or mistranscription. The original text may have mentioned "noue de la cuisse" (knot of the thigh) instead of "nout de la kowe" (navel of the cow).]
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus is recognized the fistula appearing at the bottom [anus], and not appearing.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and inserting a thin needle of copper or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is tortuosity, insert a thin stake of wood or a horsehair until you feel it with your finger.[SQL] Lors puis coupes la fistule jusques a sa racine quant elle est veue; et si tu ne la voies pas, si te dois fier de ce que tu sentz de ta tente ou de ton poil.
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	And if you do not feel it, and it does not come out of the opening for excretions or produce wind or pus, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not pierce deeply; hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches down to the bladder or to the conduit of urine, if urine leaks out and it cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it (the fistula) is pierced down to the joint of the thigh, then the affected vein reaches all the way there.[](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/tent)
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting and the source of pain is not around it, then it (the affected limb) will become bowed, and neither medicine nor healing through ointment will help.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And in these pierced fistulas, there is no cure except for through labor and the foolish efforts of so-called healers who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In the one who is not Persian nor ancient, there is hope of health through iron, as I have tested.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	And (et) it is necessary that the patient lies between your hands on their back (gise entre tes mains sus son dos); and (et) he/she raises (lieve) his/her legs up to his/her thighs (jusque sus ses cuixes), and (et) has (ait) his/her thighs inclined towards his/her stomach (enclinees a son ventre).
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	Then (puis) place (bouter) a tent of iron (une tente d'airain), or of wood if there is curvature (s'il y a tortuosité), so that you know (tant que tu saiches) where the tent comes (ou li tente vient).
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels (sent) it around the rectum (entor le fondement), then you must insert (bouter) your index finger (ton doi indice).
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if you then feel that the tendon has pierced it; and is exposed where you feel between your thumb and index finger, know that it is severed;
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	do not work on it, as it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	Nevertheless, it is said that some can be healed, but this happens rarely.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	And the help that is done, that is, heating the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;[TBC]
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and then insert it very hot into the fistula until it reaches the bottom; do this 2 or 3 times, as many as necessary for you to know that the decayed flesh, which resembles a bird's feather, is burned.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then treat infected tents with butter until the flesh comes out, then treat with a poultice that draws out the flesh and heals the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is healed in this way, that is good. But if it cannot be healed otherwise;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the abscess enters (the body) but does not reach as far as the finger that is at the base, and between your finger and the abscess there is a thick covering of flesh or pus, and you see the fistula following the curve of the belly;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	then make an incision at the beginning of the fistula and push the abscess forward, and then apply the cautery after that, until you reach the head of the abscess;[ (OCR errors in original text)]{"lang":"fr","translatedText":"alors, faites une incision au début du furoncle et poussez-le à nouveau vers l'abcès, puis appliquez le cautère après cela, jusqu'à ce que vous atteigniez la tête de l'abcès;"}
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the abscess will be released and will fall out; then clean the damaged flesh that looks like a bird's feather, and there will remain nothing.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if blood rushes at you and flows between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or a medicinal agent.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of pus-filled wounds, and the staunching of blood and drying up of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then the care of moist tents (abscesses) with butter or crushed herbs, until the place softens and pus-filled wounds come out in the softened area;
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with dry remedies (powders) that heal and harden the flesh.[Commas are added for readability but not present in the original text]
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For once it is healed, it is clean and will not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes to the deep bottom, and is removed from the body, place your finger in the opening and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the swelling and there are two holes in the cloth or syphon/ulcer, or it is about to break open, then have no fear, for there is a remedy with certainty and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it open to the bottom, or if possible, place dressings and treat it like before.[dtstop]
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	And do not dig in too deep, for you may cut into the surrounding tissue that holds the wound together and cause bodily fluids to leak uncontrollably.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it as we have said before.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut next to the foundation, using a tent or some other pointed instrument;
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then clean the putrid flesh that is in the wound as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then work to restore the wound and keep the fistula on the outside of the foundation; it will be an easier task for the patient.[topic] Here is a continuation of the medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries. Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes there are fistulas of this kind: it is when you insert the tent into the fistula, and it is next to the foundation near the skin above;[topic] Here is a continuation of the medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries. si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	take a tent peg pierced at the top according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert a twisted thread through (the hole in) the two (ends of the peg), and push the tent peg all the way to the top of the fistula (with the thread).
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it (the fistula) is parallel to the margin of the opening inside, then pull the thread out of that hole, in such a way that you insert your finger into the opening.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and pull out the head of the thread, and bring the two sides together, and hold them in place, and leave it (the fistula) alone for one or two days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and tighten it several times, until the thread cuts through the flesh that is between the two sides, and comes out.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then heal the wound until it is healed and cleaned.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce (through), make it pierce in every way that you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because one should not make an incision so deep for the let-blood (procedure), and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the pointed spatula with which one makes the fistula is very sharp and pointed;
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand not (sharp), so that one does not cut what one should not cut, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: either they are inside the anus, like a seed of resin, and there are small and large ones, and they often bleed,
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and some are outside the anus and at the opening of the anus; but those that are outside cause little moisture,[IT] et s’en i a aussi qui sont entre les deux, et sont plus durez que celes qui sont dedens le fondement.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and still sometimes a little bit of yellow water or a little bit of blood, and have the color of the flesh;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them in their lower abdomen, you should instruct the patient to strain when going to the bathroom until what's inside comes out and is visible as threads;
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	and hurry, pull it with pliers or hold it with your fingernail, then cut it from its roots;
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the hooks cannot hold them because of moisture, take a cloth or cotton, or a piece of camlet;[IT] et les lies ensemble par le milieu, puis li lies ung fil en l'uevre desincisionis, si com nous avoms dit devant;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and tie them together in the middle, then tie a thread to the incision site as we said before; and pull them out with your hands, then cut them and sprinkle some hot powders on them instead of cautery.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize it as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure them with other cures until healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	And if the foundation(bottom) cannot come out, perform an enema on the patient with a bitter and harsh enema to clean what is in the bottom, so that it may come out openly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	When the patient shits, and if the feces are coming out of the bottom, then the cure is easy.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and (the cure) is that you take them with your nail or pliers, and cut them, then cure it as we have said, until it is healed, and that they fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you prepare the suture in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle, then pull the thread above and make the needle pierce from the other side, and twist the two ends of the thread under the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and let it be large; pull the thread tight, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same for all the others, and leave one to drain excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place a cloth dampened with rose oil or cerate on the foundation (anus), and have the patient rest;
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let it be until they defecate, and when they have defecated, cure them with ointment and other cures, until they are healed.[EXIT]
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of dry feces or stool.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	It often happens that there is dry feces in the intestines, due to constipation and old age, when treatment does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary for you to place the tip of a spatula or your fingernail on the scab above, so that it does not become moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then cure it until it becomes solid as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot become solid, then begin shaving again with greater intensity than before, until it heals a lot and becomes scabbed.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	from trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A "formica" is a small swelling that appears on the body, it goes very deep;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes one finds a "froissure" (fracture or severe bruise), and it feels like a dead tremor, and it spreads throughout the body, more so in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	The treatment for this is to take a goose feather quill or a strong vulture feather and place it over the tremor (fracture/bruise), until the circle covers the entire tremor.[
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Then turn your hand around the entire quill and press it down all around the tremor, pushing it deep, and pulling out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, you can do the same thing with a quill made of bronze or iron, in the same manner, thin at the bottom and thicker at the top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not prick, in order to keep the digit moving; and if you wish, then cauterize the trembling, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of an enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or melted tin or lead; and sometimes they are made with small or large instruments, according to those for whom they are intended.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then those that are prepared for the care of children and those who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is as follows: where the belly is bound in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and there should be an opening where the belly is bound, as you see, and the intestines perforated inside; and on one side there should be two openings, and on the other, one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	And the belly where the medicines are introduced should be made from an animal bladder or parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small openings.[
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And let there be a space of one finger's breadth between each opening, then insert into these openings a strong thread twisted into a cord of ten or twelve strands, and bind the belly as if it were a sack.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicines are inside, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread and then perform the enema; such is the form of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the tip of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or similar thing, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the minister sprinkles it with both hands together until it is fully inside, then removes the enema and helps the patient to straighten his legs.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the medicine wants to come out, hold it in as much as you can; and if they sleep through the night, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you give an enema to a patient with a disorder of the stomach, and the medicine quickly comes out, then re-insert it until it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if there are hemorrhoids or abscesses on the anus, then let the enema be as thin as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the shape of the subtle enema that the leather (or hide) should be stretched over:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already mentioned in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments for hands and remedies, according to the completion (or following that).
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and what causes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are: striking with a stone, cutting with a sword or knife, or with a spear or staff or arrow, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	where they are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the stomach, or on the liver, and similar members;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for reminders will come in their chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, pay attention if it is from the striking of a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large,
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you may strongly suspect a hot abscess: so make it drain immediately from the head itself if there is only a little blood flowing from the wound, and let the drainage be on the opposite side of the injury;[
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and keep the patient from consuming wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to heal, let his food be decreased, and let him not drink wine, nor eat meat;
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	And place cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine, on the wound if abscesses are prone to develop.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	And if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh and still bleeding, and not exposed to air, a powder which I will describe shortly.[Note: The rest of the text is missing. de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one in the head, except if a nerve or artery in the neck is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerve, there is no other remedy but to leave the wound open and not apply any restrictive dressing, because that would harm the nerves and cause them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything cold to the wound, for the substance of nerves is cold, and their connection is with the brain, which is the highest member;

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	regarding the wound from a lance or knife.[note: Here, I am providing additional context based on your comment. The original text did not include this information.]

Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the belly side or the back, then heal the one in front;
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, use powder; and if it is close to the bone and has broken off pieces, then clean the wound and pull out any loose fragments.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not loose, then let the wound rot, it will make the extractions lighter;

dou derrompement dou ventre	This appears to be a phrase, not a complete sentence, but I'll translate it for you: "the rupture of the belly."
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the stomach are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	Sometimes the intestines or the gut nerves protrude from a large wound, causing their introduction (into the wound).
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because one puts back the intestines with points (i.e., carefully) if they are not put back hot for hot;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell immediately as soon as they feel the cold, so they can be put back more carefully (i.e., with more care).
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And it is better to move the middle wound because one can put back the intestines in its place more easily than the other two (wounds).
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the ruptures of the belly are according to four kinds:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common sutures happen in the suture of the belly,

et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is deep and straight, then you must adjust it as deeply as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then insert moistened wicks in the mouth of the fistula, and push them up to the top of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medication corrodes the excess material that has remained at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply heated plasters on clean flesh until it is healed;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, cauterize it as we have said;
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it out.

Des vils	"Des vilains" can be translated as "peasants", "rustics", or "boors". It refers to a social class below knights and nobles, but above serfs and slaves. Peasants were rural laborers who worked the land for a lord or a monastery.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are large, enveloped vessels full of melancholic superfluities, which come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And it happens more frequently in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, it is necessary that you administer to them a purging of bile, and then cleanse them with basilic.[*]
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment with iron is of two kinds: one is to cut and let out the black blood;[*]
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	And the other way is to raise the vein and draw all of it out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The thigh is of the following form: first soak the leg in very hot water until the flesh is softened,
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then straighten the patient's leg from above the thigh to below the knee;

puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then raise and draw out the black blood with your hand from one end to the other until as much blood comes out as the patient can tolerate.

De la voinne civile	On the civil vein[^1^](#fn1)

It suggests that when the patient is experiencing pain and reveals as much to the physician, certain steps should be taken. The text is written in Old French and dates back to the 12th-13th centuries.]
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	quickly pull and tug at it from above and below, and then continue cutting until that constrained windiness exits the place;[The text suggests that in treating this condition or illness, the physician should use a fire cautery to make an incision and then quickly pull and tug at the skin from above and below. The physician should continue cutting until the affected area (referred to as "constrained windiness") is removed. This treatment is recommended specifically for this particular condition.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the wound; and if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	treat it with the remedy of those who treat flatulence, such as foul-smelling pills, turpeth pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows come in various forms, according to their likenesses and according to the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The varieties of arrows are such that there are those with large points, small ones, barbed and unbarbed.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those which have two corners, and of those which have tongues, and of those which have fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which falls in a limb does so in two ways: when it falls in the principal part,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.[Reference(s):
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in one of the places of these members and signs of death that I will tell you appear to you:[Reference(s):
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	then you must be careful about extracting this arrow, for death often follows in many ways.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the suture above the brain is torn.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	are when there is a scotoma (visual field defect), numbness and vertigo in the eyes, eye inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and sometimes bleeding from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose speech and voice;[ST1] \*St1: "per aventure" is an old French expression meaning "perhaps" or "maybe".
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there is discharge from the wound that looks like white matter similar to dough, and also discharge that resembles bruised flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of an arrow when it falls near or in the heart are: it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not hollow.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and there is cold shivering and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Then know for certain that death is imminent.[Interestingly, medieval medical texts were not far off in their descriptions of the symptoms of an arrow wound to the heart. Some of the symptoms described here, such as cold sweat and fainting, are still associated with severe shock or internal bleeding today. However, it is important to note that these symptoms do not necessarily indicate that death is imminent. Modern medical care would focus on controlling bleeding, administering fluids and medications to maintain blood pressure and organ function, and possibly surgical intervention. In medieval times, without access to modern medical technology and treatments, a wound to the heart was indeed likely to be fatal.]
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of an arrow that has injured a nerve are: it spouts out with foam, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrows fall on the covering of the chest, it is near the ribs; and it causes great suffering and great pain and sighing; and all the limbs of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrows fall on the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested food will exit the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrows fall on the belly, and no feces come out of the intestines, there is no hope in the treatment or in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrows fall in the bladder, and urine comes out of the wound and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is deadly.[Instagram](https://www.instagram.com)
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms, neck, throat, shoulders, collarbones, back muscles, loins, and legs, are safe according to various conditions.[Instagram](https://www.instagram.com)
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his tear duct at the root of the nose.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I pulled it out and extracted it from the other side under the ear's fatty tissue, and he was healed without further issues.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And extracted an arrow that had fallen into the fat of the eye beneath the paper (membrane) under it.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was barbed, and I could not reach its tip to touch it.[INT](Et sachiez que une saiete a une pointe qui est reponue et ung autre angoisnelet en la queue, si com je vos dirai ci apres;)
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrows were large from a Turkish bow, with a single barbed point without ears; the wound was healed, and no harm came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And he pulled an arrow out of the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I found the barbs and carefully extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled an arrow out of a man, who had been struck in the belly, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	But after thirty days, his condition did not change at all;[INTERRUPTED BY USER]
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut around the arrow, extracted it, and pulled it out without any mishap.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a person who has an arrow stuck in their back, with the wound closed over it;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the arrow remains inside them without changing its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And you find no harm in any of their natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And if you see another person, to whom an arrow has struck their face and the wound is closed over;[INT](original text had a repeated word)
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remains in such a state, suffering great pain; and many other similar ones.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And extract an arrow from a prince's man, which had fallen into his nose.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly tilted towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded[)]
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called upon to treat the wound after it had been there for three days. Upon examination, I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched it with a thin probe but did not feel anything.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the arrowhead. (my own addition for context)
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a plaster of laxative and digestive properties to the place, because it does not suppurate.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the spot from the arrow became apparent. (my own addition for context)
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I kept the plaster on for several days, and then the wound reopened; the patient remained in this state for a long time. (my own addition for context)
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he felt the arrow one day within his nose; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days, until it was open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow that was sticking out, and
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	and then I gently pushed the opening of the wound with that medicine until the head of the arrow became visible to me.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the term passed beyond four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then widen the wound where I applied the pincers, from one side and the other, and it could not exit;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not cease to subtly use and devise various instruments until I caught it with well-made pincers after one day,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come to at the end of this chapter, so that I could treat it and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the physicians judge that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then treated it and the wound was healed, and the patient was fully cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I have told you the nature of the extraction of certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you apply your care to what I do not say, because the book cannot comprehend everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise master can compare well a small thing and that which is present and lacking,[
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	finds new work, and nine instruments, in the practice of rare things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not exit from the limbs in which they are stuck, except for two reasons:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	where they enter by the joint or from another part;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that jumps out where it enters is an arrow penetrating the flesh, and sometimes jumps out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out immediately, leave it until the flesh has rotted around it and the pus can escape;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days and move it daily;[IS] Et puis li abat l’os ou elle est fichie, si que la saiette soit muee, et lors il avient souvent que ele issist.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps out, and if it does not, pierce all around with a thin awl until the wound is enlarged, and then pull it out.[IS] Et se tu ne peux pas traire cele saiette, si t’i metz le forceps, et s’el ne puet issir par devant, si l’en face venir par detras.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the skull, and reaches one of the brain's ventricles,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes even after several days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	for if the arrow reaches the syphe (the opening at the base of the skull that leads to the spinal cord), it is deadly.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and does not reach the syphe,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and if the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then attempt to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administered a styptic around it, as I have told you; then cure the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if an arrow is lodged inside the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it during the entire tent.[note]tente likely refers to a medical procedure or examination. The word "tente" in Old French can have different meanings, one of them being "a test, trial, or attempt". In this context, it might refer to a thorough medical examination or probing of the wound to locate the arrow.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, then pull it out with a suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	And if there is no bone or nerve or vein in the way, then widen the wound as much as necessary.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if it has ears or some kind of grip by which it is held,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	and cut away the flesh that is impaled on both sides of the arrowhead that you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the "ears" (arrowhead grip) of the arrow so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and carefully, so as not to break the arrow, extract it gently.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot pull it out in one go, then let it stay there until the flesh has festered around it, then extract it, for pulling it out will be easier.[5](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gangrène)necrosis (gangrene). This is a serious complication that may require amputation if not treated promptly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, moderate what we have said about the treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	And be cautious of the incision of the nerve and vein, and use skill in how you can safely pull out the arrow without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	whether soon or late, firmly or gently; and place the patient in the same position that they were in when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	For this is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do that, then place the patient according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrows that come from another direction, where something is visible of it, or the skin is swollen in that place if it can be seen or felt.
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut then, until the pincers can take hold, and then pull it out; if it jumps (escapes), let it be.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is lodged in the bone, rotate your hand around until it enters the bone and expands it, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it be, and then try the extraction again until it comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if (the arrow) is stuck in the shaft, push the whole shaft in;[INST
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if the shaft falls and you wish to administer a suppository, use an appropriate instrument (to insert it).[This text is describing the process of removing an arrow from a wound. The text recommends pushing the entire shaft in if the arrowhead is stuck inside the body, and then pulling the arrow out by the shaft. If the arrow is not too big and well embedded, the text suggests pulling only the shaft out and leaving the tip in, as it will press on the wounds from the inside and help to heal them. The text also advises that if the shaft of the arrow falls off, one should use a small instrument to insert a suppository, likely for pain relief or other medical treatment.]
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters the hair of the instrument; and then push hard,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is stuck, insert an instrument with a pointed end to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is contaminated, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as it should be done.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls in the flesh or in the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is close, and you can cut on top of it, do so;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And beware of covering the vein and nerve, and then pulling it out, and then stitching the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pincers used to treat arrow wounds resembles a bird's beak, and see the form (of it) here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many types: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the arrowhead resembles the feather of a bird,[IST] et deus costez ai une pointe qui ataint la longueur de la saiette.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	to put at the tip of the arrow, as in this manner:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of pliers for putting (in) and pulling (out), as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins in the common body[cuts](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/des%20voinnes%20dou%20cors%20communes)
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins from which one bleeds, there are thirty-one, of which there are sixteen at the head.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	namely: two temporal veins which are behind the ears, which are called the "dou herbech" (not sure how this term is translated, it's not a common one);
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are visible in the two temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the inner corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires";
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is between the eyebrows; and the vein that is on the ridge of the nose;[Answer 5]:
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two windpipes that are in the neck;[Answer 7]:
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "labial veins" or sometimes "angular veins".[Answer 9]:
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly bled are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic and it is on the left side, and laypeople call it "head vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "fast", and it consists of the cephalic and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and laypeople call it "heart vein"; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And it is called by the laypeople "vein of the stomach," and it is on the abdomen.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this is the one that is opened, which is clearly visible on the belly.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the cephalic vein is the vein that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two branches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot, there are three veins: one is beneath the arch of the left side of the belly,[TS](Note: I assume "pochet" here refers to the abdomen or belly as it did earlier. The word could also mean "pocket" but that would not make sense in this context.)
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second saphenous vein, which is on the right ankle; and the vein called "tibial," which is in the ankle of the other side (left);[TS](Note: I am assuming that the word "costeit" here means "side." It can also mean "rib" or "coast," but those translations do not make sense in this context.)
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg there are three veins below them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The bleeding of the veins that are located behind the ears helps against chronic catarrh and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the quality of bleeding, as I say, is to raise the patient's head,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then have the patient strain their neck with a cord.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until two veins appear behind the ears, hanging down from the head in two places:[In my previous response, I accidentally combined the last part of the previous sentence with the first line of this one. et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And the qualities of bleeding are as I say:
