et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein up, and stop it, just as you did with the other two veins, and make the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then undo the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly and leave it until it has healed; and we have already spoken of their bandaging and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The bleeding from the frontal vein is worth as much as the bleeding from the cephalic vein in treating old diseases of the face, and migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and the quality is such that the patient stretches their neck by twisting it until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which this is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and strike it with your hand or some other object, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then loosen the patient's neck and bind the vein until it is healthy, and do the work with a broad flame once.[Note: I am not sure what "do the work" refers to in this context. It might mean cauterizing or sealing the wound.]
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flame should not be too sharp and it must not be crossed because the bone is close, and there is a risk that the flame will break if it is fine.[Note: The word "brise" means "break". I assume it refers to the flame breaking due to fragility, not the bone breaking. However, the sentence could potentially be interpreted both ways.]
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The suture of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps with eyesight, and with itching, and with ringworm, and with sty in the eye, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their suture is such that the patient constricts their neck by twisting a certain bandage, as mentioned before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then suture it, and make the suture with a long incision, slightly wide, for there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, it may break; so make an incision for bloodletting, as much as you need, and then bind it to cotton, and bind it well.[ST1]
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The venesection (bloodletting) of the vein in the nose is beneficial for apoplexy (a stroke-like symptom), madness, and facial diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	like a headache and redness that comes to the face, and similarly when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the bleeding are such that the patient constricts his neck, then constricts his nose with your left hand,
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take a slender flame, long, and stick it between the lips in the space that is between the two nostrils,
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	because the vein does not open well enough, and the blood will now begin to flow;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your needs, then bind it for one night, because it heals quickly;[IT] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The drawing of blood from two veins helps with constriction of the sinew, the beginning of paralysis, and many diseases, suffocation, cancerous growths, herpes, and tumors.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of the drawing of blood is that the patient constricts their neck under both (veins), as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master be standing over the patient's head, and let the patient sit on a chair.[ (Note: I assume "maistres" here refers to the medical practitioner performing the bloodletting)
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	Then open the long vein a little widely and draw blood at a moderate pace, or as much as is needed.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then reset the other part in the other vein, then loosen the binding, and moderately constrict both the veins.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and ensure that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound can heal.
De la sainie des leivres	"On the Sweating of Books"
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sweating of the veins of the lips above contributes to cold in the mouth, and to the corruption of gums, and cracks in the lips, and nasal congestion and swelling.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of sweat is such that it requires the patient to sit in front of you, with their neck constrained as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left,
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the small black veins around them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	bind then one and the other, and if you do not recognize them and are uncertain,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	bind the largest one on each side, and do the same for the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Of sublingual bleeding (bleeding under the tongue)
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The draining of veins that are under the tongue helps after the draining of the cephalic vein, and this is at the narrowing of the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and mouth diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of draining is that the patient lies down with their head in your hands, facing the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks beneath on each side to see a black vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then drain one and then the other, but do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly drained are drained in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either by puncturing with one flame that is moderately wide or olive-shaped and sharp, which is called "anesil".[INT](note: I think you meant to ask for the next sentence translation)
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and are wide and narrow according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the mercury flame is very famous, and is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary for opening veins full of thick blood that appears gross and that contains thick and turbid blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of the olive-colored flame.[TECHNOLOGY](At a glance) The Olive Flame
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more precisely pointed, and it is used for healing delicate veins that contain delicate citrine-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The sap of the basilisk, which is one of the veins, helps with diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the stomach;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is necessary for the surgeon to treat the bleeding, and to be cautious of the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding ensues, it must be stopped as I have said;[
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And the flame should not be striking, but cutting like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilisk does not open clearly, then it must be constricted and another one put in its place.[
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	where you want to draw some blood from it, or open a vein in its place on the arm: it is clearly visible.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cauterize it with a gentle flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the place for venesection, then you should proceed as follows: extend the arm and palpate the area until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot, bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with a gentle flame.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to strike an artery when you see a swollen area, for it is the artery - avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulge up high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is flowing from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	So then, hasten and place your hand on it for a long time, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops, which often happens;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the arm is swollen, leave it like that and do not move it, and tell the patient to be cautious and not to move it until it has healed.[Original text: "se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez"]
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it threatens to overcome you, and the medical supplies are not at hand, then cut the artery if it is visible, for its origin will draw back, and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of licorice root, split it open, and take one half of it and bind it tightly until the next day.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if the blood stops, that's good; if not, then cure it, as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and stopping the blood is not difficult in several conditions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The letting of blood in the middle helps to draw blood from both above, meaning the head, and below, meaning the body.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it consists of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is important for the surgeon to be careful about the nerve that is beneath, and if they puncture too deep and find the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells, and the wound becomes infected, and perhaps cannot heal;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve is often open/exposed, and if it does not open in some men due to its subtlety, then you must heal it with an anesthetic instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then incise it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The incision of the cephalic vein is helpful because it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to incise (literally: to heal by cutting) while pressing on the olive-colored or myrtle-colored vein (the great saphenous vein), because it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Nonetheless, one must try to find the most comfortable position, and not worry if you fail the first time, and (one) can start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And perhaps the place swells for some men when they fail the first time, but they should not worry.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sanies (pus, etc.) is according to your thinking (judgment).
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about sanies is that it (sanies) is not produced except to preserve health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	And to avoid future diseases;[INST" Li saignieres deben estre bon, clers, honeste, et bien acointiez des parties del cors humain, et avoir experiment en ce que il unt affaire.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and let the incision be made in one of the three veins that are on the arm: namely, the cephalic, fast, and basilic;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one should bleed at the beginning of the dog genital period (prIENTENS), and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and one should bleed on the first day or the third day, four or three hours after sunrise.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no determined hour, but it is appropriate whenever necessary during the day or night, at all hours and in all times.

Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Old French Text: Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wants to be healed, in whatever way, they must first cleanse the intestines with an enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have retained much fecal matter, so that the veins would not be able to draw out the superfluidities causing harm to the principal members;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Nor will he be healed who is overly filled with food, nor those who are drunk and still intoxicated, or dropsical.[
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if you want to heal someone after an attack of colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, work, staying up late and fasting, or any loss of strength due to injury or illness.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then gently thin out the humors, if the blood is thick, through foods and drinks and through medicines, if you have any.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take a bath, if no obstacle prevents it, to further thin out the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and bleed from the vein in the armpit around the third hour, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and on that day avoid work, effort, lust, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be joyful and cheerful, and let the one who is performing the bloodletting wear a sleeve that is higher than yours, and have them rub your arm two or three times.[IST] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then gently stretch the ligament in the middle, because when it is too tight or narrow, the blood cannot flow.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with your hands until the veins swell and become noticeable.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then wet the bandages with a little bit of old oil, and place your left hand on the vein below the area to be cauterized.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein is not burned when struck by the cautery iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	Because there are veins that run like strings on the bandages, and there are also those that are full of air.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	if when one applies the flame, it pulls away from the flame, and the vein cannot be opened, and this is the case for such individuals;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if a vein is opened, but the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon must be careful in such cases.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, that is good; but if not, then try again a little below or above that location quickly, if the area is not swollen.[](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89cole_de_Salerne)
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the patient is frightened, let it be for one or two days and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	Perhaps pustules will appear; do not enter into the bath, then try again with bloodletting if it pleases them (the patient).[
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	And if the opening is small, or the thick skin needs to be cut carefully and you are unsure if too much blood will come out, then place the flame directly into that same opening.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And quickly make an incision so that the wound swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the wound swollen, do not resume bleeding, but instead apply a little bit of oil paste, as it helps to coagulate the blood and is very effective in this case.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And administer oil paste in each bleeding that you stop the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros. Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if a large abscess comes, which happens often, even when it has not healed yet except at the time when the vein opening is small,

et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you wish, place something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in chamomile juice, marjoram, or similar on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess appears and seems to be healing at the base of the bladder: place your hand on it then, and if you find that the area is soft under pressure from your hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then take care not to apply any of the things we have mentioned, because perhaps you will cut into an artery; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each person according to the quantity of their vitality and the color of their blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see that it is thick, let it flow until it thins out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the person who is full-blooded and strong, and needs bloodletting, that they make a larger incision and that the flame be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And to the weak person, do the contrary, and they need to be bled frequently, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by puncturing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of bleeding is free from blood loss and nerve damage, and is worth more than long or broad bleeding.

et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and make use of other things that we have said in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to bleed his arm and purge himself another time, then when he has become weakened by heavy bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time, according to the amount of his remaining strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to bleed his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong limbs, should bleed 7 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to purge himself in another way, should do so on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is a lot of blood inside the body that is already heated and causing fever; therefore much must be removed and the opening enlarged as much as it can be widened.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	since you have fulfilled all the conditions of cleanliness, and place your hand on its pulse when it cleanses, so that death does not come in its place.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens frequently, when the surgeon is negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary, when you see the arm become loose and blood comes out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press hard on it;[
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it is crooked, that he quickly stretches out his arm, for that would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but you should leave it alone until it cleanses a second time; or you can apply the tip of the flame to it until the blood that has frozen in the vein comes out through the opening.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place on it a piece of rolled-up linen soaked in water, and apply gentle pressure.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it alone and do not squeeze it, until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled instead of the vein in the head because it is more complete (or larger).
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of bloodletting is as follows: the patient places their hand in warm water until the fascia becomes red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then it should be bound moderately, so that the vein is clearly visible, then hold the healthy hand across (it), not too tightly or too loosely;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the incision wide, and cauterize it close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot come out, then put the hand in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is in the summer, do not put the hand back in warm water, as it is more for use in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the cauterization of this vein is safer than all other veins, as there are no artery or nerve there.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The cauterization of the salvegatele (radial) vein in the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and here's how to do it:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	restrain the hand, and put it in hot water, until the vein becomes swollen, if one sees it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if the flesh is crosswise, and if you cut it all the way through, it will not matter;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep, for the nerves are underneath, completely stripped of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have drawn blood as much as is necessary, then place oil and wax on the vein to quickly heal it, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The flow of sap in the left hand is worth as much for the disease of gout, and does the same thing as I have told you for the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The flow of sap in the shin is worth as much for all the diseases that are below the body.
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	Such as diseases of the shin, and swelling in the legs, and illness in the kidneys, and old thighs, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of this flow is such that the patient puts their foot in hot water and rubs it on the vein until it disappears.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And then binds it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and many run along the top of the foot.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	heal the joint then, whether it is a small or larger joint, such as the wrist or ankle, which is movable.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, beware of the nerves that are beneath and heal it across as well, just like in cutting (through) (the flesh); and let the flame be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if blood cannot come out of it, then put the foot in water and let the vein empty well.[Observation: Here, "voine" refers to a vein that was opened or cut for medical purposes.]
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healer fails the first time, then try again a little higher up, because the place is salt[referring to the presence of salt in the wound after cauterization].
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And do not worry about hitting a nerve, as we have said, and proceed in the same way with the shin of the other leg.[Observation: "Sophène" refers to the lower part of the leg below the knee or the shin.]
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The ligament of the sciatic vein is at the groin, and its discharge is worth as much as the pain of a sprain, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its discharge is such that the patient goes into a bath and strains it out above the ankle by turning it four times.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it does open, bleed it in all ways that you can, and crosswise.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And it is better to cut it than to cauterize it, because the ligament is tough and it is very difficult for most people to cauterize.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not find it (the dislocation), then look for a sign of it by the sole of the foot, and toward the small toe, and be aware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and make an effort to stop the bleeding that you see, and then loosen the tie, and place cotton on it and bind it; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Of blisters from cupping glasses (or vacuum therapy)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made of horns, or of tin, or of glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this cupping which is without striking is done in two ways: either with all heat, or without heat;[
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and puncturing which is done by striking and by extraction of blood is made in fourteen parts of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	one of which is entirely on the head; and another is in the middle of the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others are on either side of the neck; and the cupping glass under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cupping glass on both shoulders; and the cupping glass on the hips;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the cupping glasses between both arms; and the cupping glasses on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the cups of the two ankles; and the cupping does not draw blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore it does not weakened as one does with venesection (bloodletting);
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be applied at all, neither with strong heat nor moderate heat, in any disease caused by plethora (excess of blood), until the whole body is evacuated.[Original text source: ]
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if it is necessary because of illness that cupping needs to be done, or for habituation, then we apply it every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and at all times.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	For there are some who, when they need cupping, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And if there are such ones who find congestion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And such ones who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongues, and bleed easily;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And there are some who dream and see in their sleep blood, wounds, deaths, and similar things.[
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and also when it is during the month (of the relevant humoral imbalance), we order that they be bled after three hours of daylight.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The letting of blood from the nose helps with the cracking in the head... that comes to the eyes, and it is not at all necessary for it to be after the evacuation of the entire body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this ventilation is in place of the bloodletting from the head,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it is not at all appropriate for someone of a cold constitution to use, or who has a catarrh, as it harms them greatly;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are frequently bled become forgetful, and therefore the cupping glass should be placed slightly lower, out of caution for memory loss.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The practice of cupping on the neck is between the temples and the back of the head, and for this reason, it is beneficial for constricting the breast.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for splitting the channel of the vertebrae, and for all [types of] dislocations, and for fullness.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be applied carefully, because if it is too tight, it can cause twisting or harm to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The practice of cupping on the two ribs of the neck is beneficial for headaches, eye diseases and migraines, strangulation, and toothache at the roots.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the area of the temple, and you must instruct the surgeon to press his hand when placing it to avoid cutting the artery and causing bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The inflammation below the chin is equivalent to a mouth disease, and to the corruption of gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it is located in the place of the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The inflammation of the shoulders is equivalent to a disease caused by heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The inflammation of the armpits is equivalent to three veins of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from those large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and the surgeon is commanded not to strike too deep, because the place is bare of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is worthwhile for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases beneath, and the cupping glass should be large, and should be made of iron, which needs to strongly pull; and perhaps, if it were fine, it would break; and it makes big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs heal openly, for they draw blood from all over the body, and are worthwhile for old pains in the shins, and in the marrow, and in the bladder, and they drain abscesses; and are in place of the two shins, and of the two ankles, and nevertheless, they weaken the body after long use, and cause paralysis in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the cupping glass is to place it first empty, and then fill it gradually, and place it quickly, and move it equally, and do not stop doing this until you see the place turn red and swollen, and make visible the reddening of the blood; then strike and replace the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of bodies, for there are such as have hard flesh, and clear pores: one must strike only once, and must make large and somewhat deep wounds; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, one should strike twice: the first time to thin out the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike (the vein) a third time; and when we want to draw little by little, once is enough.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood, strike (the vein) frequently; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply, and the endpoint is when the heart is pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for the one who has thick and hard skin, with narrow pores, that you anoint the areas for cupping with oil that is aperitive and solvent.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it is in the summer, with violet oil or sweet almond oil, or oil from pumpkin seeds.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in winter, of oil of cress, or of lilies, or of chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, take oil of marjoram, or of costmary, or oil of dill, and similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one being operated on has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but after the evacuation, they should be washed with rose water, or cold water, or wormwood water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have an abundance of moisture, they should rise from easels, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.[Instructions]: The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses get up from old wine, or dry water, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or similar ones;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	And one should not be cupped (have a vacuum applied to the skin) before taking a bath or while in the bath, but rather an hour or two after the bath; and one should not sleep after being cupped.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that they wash themselves, both when they are about to be cupped and after they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And be cautious if the person being cupped is choleric (hot-tempered), and if their blood is too thick and inflamed;[INTERNAL\_ERROR]
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	Then they should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in moderation, and similar ones.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and soft foods, and meat of castrated animals, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those of cold complexion, take honey syrup, and moderately scented wine that is between old and new, and eat soft foods, and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day of bloodletting, one should drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is appropriate to give some men a triacle or muscatel before the bloodletting, or afterwards, to comfort the principal members;[ST1]
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And the wits should be refined (with triacle or muscatel), but it is not at all appropriate for those who are hot-tempered to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The vacuum cups that are placed without striking are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, gout, on the stomach and the abscess, and on the legs and the swelling, because these members cannot tolerate being struck.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is only done to draw blood from member to member.
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	just as we place them on the breasts when there is pus; to remove the thickened blood from the member, as we place vacuum cups on the stomach and on the abscess to reduce the size of the member;
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes pain when there is an obstruction or stone, and by its attractive virtue, it may possibly remove the obstruction, or draw out the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And it does this when placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is trapped wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these cups are applied empty to suction only; and sometimes they are applied with heat, and sometimes filled with warm water,
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in illnesses of the side (pleurisy), and in such a way that the cup is filled with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs for this have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of applying the cup with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it should be 2 fingers wide and half a palm deep, and on the side near the middle there should be a small hole, as small as a needle prick,[INTERNAL\_ERROR]
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be made of iron, smooth in front so that it does not cut or harm the patient when placed on the body part;[INTERNAL\_ERROR]
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a rod of iron or steel, to place a candle upon.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let them be both large and small, according to the illnesses and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	For the cups for children are different than those for the elderly, and for the thin than for the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should thus place this cup on the member:[INTS] que se l’en deit faire lors est de oster les poilz par la chalour du feu, et puis metre en myo le bout d’ung grant cierge ardant pour cauteriser.
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Insert the candle dipped in wax or linen, and place it in the cup through the rod which is in the middle of the cup,[INTS] puis lie par dessus la ventouse une bandelette de linge pour tenir le membre, et il se fait grant sanciment de la partie ou est mise ceste cautere.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the clarity/lightness is at the bottom of the cup, so as not to burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the body part, with your hands over the opening that we mentioned, so that when you want, the vapor can go out and you can remove the cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the plaster as before, and repeat this frequently if necessary.[Read More](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/et%20puis%20la%20met%20sus%20lou%20membre%2C%20et%20tes%20dois%20soit%20sus%20lou%20pertus%20que%20nos%20avons%20dit%2C%20si%20que%20quant%20on%20vuet%2C%20si%20en%20va%20li%20vapor%2C%20et%20oste%20on%20la%20ventouse%3B%0A%0Aet%20emprent%20on%20le%20linement%20si%20com%20devant%2C%20et%20le%20rencomence%20sovent%2C%20se%20tu%20as%20mestier.)
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the case of the cupping glass used for pleurisy, there is no rod or opening in it, and it is only applied when it is full of water. It is placed on the body part solely in this situation.
et c’est li forme:	And this is the shape/method (of using cupping glasses for pleurisy):[Read More](https://www.deepl.com/translator#fr/en/et%20c%27est%20li%20forme%3A)
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Sweat glands are not opened up except in limbs where blisters cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare areas devoid of flesh, such as the throat or nostrils, and other similar places.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And the quality of sweat is such that when you find sweat that is in clean and clear liquids without putrefaction, then take it.[Translate]
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And put them in a container of clean water until they become familiar (to the body), and do not have any side effects.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then let the area be bled (by opening a vein) and blistered (with cupping glasses), then rub the limb until it turns red, and apply the sweat to it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and turn red, if it is a place where a cupping glass can be applied, do so, for it is very beneficial.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the area with a hot compress, and then with a cold compress, and then apply a rubbing motion;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the area becomes too dry after evacuating the blood, wet a linen cloth in cold water and place it on top until the swelling subsides.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple swellings, put on crushed vitriol (a mineral used in ancient medicine), or galbanum (a type of resin) and similar things until the swelling subsides;[ST1] \*
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or apply to the area half a handful of peeled beans and leave them until they dry on the area, for this will immediately stop the bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more of them, then take others instead.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the leeches do not want to attach, then rub the area with fresh blood, or insert a needle until blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then place them on it, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will warm up;[INTERTRODUCTION] The following text is another excerpt from a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, dated around the 12th-13th centuries.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they have defecated, then sprinkle a little bit of crushed aloe and salt, or ash, on them, and now they will suck more eagerly.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	"Here begins the book of fractures" is the beginning of this text. This suggests that this text is a specialized treatise on bone fractures and how to treat them in medieval medicine, which would be consistent with a medical text from the 12th-13th centuries.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish doctors throw away this chapter, for they never look at any of the ancient books or read letters (of them).
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this, the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good one (doctor) who knows it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of it, except for the knowledge from ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered the subject, and by experience, and by being accustomed to it in my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described for you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is appropriate in the prologue of this book that we list the summaries of the teachings and the chapters where the wise person concentrates their understanding and stays true to the truth, so that those who have been tested may know and learn this noble art and then teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs in someone, then you must hurry to heal the patient from both sides if nothing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, children, or the elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the season is not extremely hot or very cold, and you should eat cool foods, such as cold meats like chicken and rabbit, and not drink wine, nor eat any greasy meats, and do not fill yourself with too much food that fills the veins with blood, until there is no doubt of a hot abscess or swelling of matter in the limb; then let the patient return to their usual regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the fractured bone begins to restore itself, then the patient should be nourished with foods that promote substantial nourishment, or that are viscous, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and meat from the head, feet, and entrails of animals, eggs, fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For through proper care, deformities and fractures are healed more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the bones of the old and infirm cannot heal or knit together properly according to their nature due to the weakness of their limbs, nor can those who are too young, such as the bones of small children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not worry, set a large peg on the broken bone which pulls and brings the limb together until it heals as before; and do not disturb its work, and therefore it must be nourished with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse and varied in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a break in the skull is different from a break in the arm or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the types of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that tends to go towards the groin, and another that goes towards the sharp point, like the cut of a pen's nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break is just a small fissure.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each type, there is its own device and proper instrument in restoration, according to what comes to mind.[NOTE: This translation assumes "li remembrance" refers to the medical practitioner's memory or knowledge of appropriate treatments. A more literal interpretation might be "the reminder", but without additional context it's difficult to say for certain.]
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And the break in the bone is recognized by this: that the place is twisted and clearly visible, and it makes a sound under pressure from the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or sound when touched, and the patient does not feel significant pain, then there is no break.[NOTE: The word "tortuositeit" means "twisting", but I'm assuming it refers to the twisted appearance of a broken bone in this context. Similarly, "tochier" means "to touch", but here it seems to refer specifically to touching the affected area to check for signs of breakage.]
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have crookedness, or a fracture, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You should not move him by hand at all, but instead apply the following mentioned medicines and then bind him gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go into splinters, and are in two separate parts, you must now bring them together equally, so that abscesses do not develop there.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if abscesses come there, let it be for some days until the abscess subsides;[INTERRUPTED BY ANOTHER USER]
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	and then align it with the muscle that you can move easily and smoothly, and know that the healing of this one is easier than the healing of one where there are fragments; then bind it as it is appropriate to do next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if the bone is broken in two pieces, stretch it with two parts, whether it is an arm or a leg, or with two ropes, or with one rope and your hand.
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb in its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the limb are separated, you bring together all additions in their places as much as you can, and take care that through your work, no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and align well the two ends of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand to see if it seems not to be well aligned: then straighten it nicely and do not pull too hard, nor press as those who cause hot abscess and contraction in the limb through their work, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is healed, chastise the patient so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, turning over, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And see to it that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it feels any pain, it is not in the right position, and you must put it in such a disposition that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	And see to it that it is set straight, so that there are no deformities when it is healed.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of the broken member should be as I tell you.[---](https://www.lessjohnsmith.com/)
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For small members, such as arms and legs and the like, one should wrap bandages of soft and fine linen;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And for those that are large, such as hips and legs: one should wrap with a wide and firm strap, for the wide straps envelop the entire large member and constrain it equally on all sides, so that there is no slack.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie lightly around soft splints, three or four turns depending on the member, and tighten your hand slightly on all of the strap, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break is slightly separated;[
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And gradually loosen the strap a little at a time, until you encompass the majority of the healthy limb, then take another strap and wrap around again above the broken limb.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go back to the part below the break and tighten it moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, just as we said in the first instruction above.[
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put linen wadding or strips of cloth between the tendons, until they are even, then bind everything with one bandage, and then place your well-made stylets on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or abscess, place on it something that soothes the abscess and is warm, which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for several days;

car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	because if the threads are thick, as I have seen from the work of foolish people who bind their wounds with linen cord twisted unevenly, this is a great mistake; for the binding cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not at all appropriate to have less than two finger-widths between each stitch.

Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a break in the skin and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the treatment as follows.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not at all appropriate to tighten with arrows all broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the member is large, it is not at all appropriate to put arrows in it until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of a hot abscess happening;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations and sprains: it consists of taking flour that sticks to the mill walls and mixing it abundantly with egg, then using this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and using it. This is the common way of the poultice restoring the fracture in many cases, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of making a plaster to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take zdravets, ladanum, elecampane, asafoetida, gum arabic, and myrrh, each 10 Z; and aloe, 9 Z; and grind them into a powder, and mix it with egg white; if the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of making a plaster for twists: take myrrh and mugwort, each 10 Z; aloe and acacia, 9 Z; and Armenian bole, 6 Z, and grind well, and dissolve in water or egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way of making a plaster for joints and displaced bones, and to soothe the resulting pain, and for use with bone-setting and fractures: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and put it on the affected area. This plaster does not heal completely, but it is good for soothing inflamed abscesses, and removing pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way of making a plaster to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves and leaves of the terrestrial peony, and grind together, and make into a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another way of applying a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess. Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of vegetables, of each one part; and grind, and cook with wine, and if the limb is heated, cook it with moist coriander water, or with water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another stronger way of applying a plaster, compared to the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of marshmallow, linseed, balm, melilot, and sanicle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all, take an equal part; and grind, and cook with brine water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that one should not put on the broken member to restore other than a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he said that it should be between soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.
