And it seems that Galen thinks one should put on the broken member, to restore, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.[English interpretation: Galen believes that in order to heal a fracture, one should apply warm, dry substances such as myrrh, aloes, and incense to the affected area.]
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of plaster that is valuable for wound and pain: take houseleek and chopped off human hair or bird feathers, and add wormwood and equal amounts of grease, grind them, and make a plaster and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then unbind it a little afterward, and take care if the patient does not feel any pain, and if the bones have not moved from their place; if so, do not unbind it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and unbind it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, soak them in water, and raise the area, until the itching stops, and the pain subsides.[
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Afterward, let the member rest for an hour, then place soft wool, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it to a knot, until you are sure of the abscess being hot;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then gently restart the ligature, and a little emplaster, and do not constrict it as much as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful, and has opened completely, and you need emplaster and bandages, then reapply it as you did in the beginning.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if no improvement is seen in the limb after the treatments we have mentioned, then do not release it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days, and sometimes leave it for 20 days, depending on what is observed, until the break heals and the joining of flesh begins.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then bind it more tightly than before and the flesh will fatten, as I said earlier; and if you see that the place is drying out more than necessary, know that there can be no healing.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	boil the joint in hot water each time you release it, every third day, and loosen the ligament a little;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	by this work, therefore, the blood flow to the limb is cut off and quickly corrects what foolish doctors do when they incorrectly restore the limb: it is wrong, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and work on it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	"of the different ways of fracture"
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, with various shapes and distinct causes;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	because there are fractures caused by sword blows, and the collarbone separates the entire bone down to the shaft that is underneath the bone, just like an axe or stick would do; therefore, this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a hidden impact, or a split from a stone or a fall on a stone, or from other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.[Note: The word "toile" here refers to a membrane or tissue under the skin or bone.]
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that is embedded in the bone as thin as a hair, and the split is small, and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "hairline".[Note: The word "chevous" here means hairs or very fine strands.][Stylistic note: I have used the spelling "fracture" instead of the original "brisure" to maintain consistency in terminology.]
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or by falling, and it drives a piece of bone inward, and the site appears like blisters that blacksmiths get when they hammer on cauldrons, and stones enter inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their head, such as the bones of a child;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs in all these types of fractures where small pieces are separated, such as splinters; and I will speak on that later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all types of fractures by the withdrawal (or traction) on them, and through investigation using probes, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top (of the wound).
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of a fracture (resembling hair) is recognized by this: when the bone is uncovered and rubbed against, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the patient's condition and if you see any adverse symptoms, such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, swelling, paleness, feverishness, eyes becoming exserted and red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then it cannot be healed without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for recovery, then begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the bone within the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, you should quickly remove the bone within the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone does not become corrupt and the accidents that we have mentioned do not occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, you must split open the affected part in this way: that is, take hold of the head of the wounded person and expose the bone as much as you can, and as gently as possible on the surface of the wound
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if bleeding occurs when the bone is exposed or an abscess arises, use what is necessary and fill the wound with cloths soaked in rose oil
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	and let the wound rest until the abscess has subsided, and you are assured of proper blood flow; then begin around the bone to remove [the pus], and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and its shape is:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision that is larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is to have multiple incisions of varying sizes, some narrow and others wide, with sharp points, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.[In this context, "head" refers to the pus-filled abscess or swelling that needs to be drained. The text advises making multiple incisions of different sizes and shapes, some narrow and others wide, with sharp points, and made of iron, and to do so carefully and skillfully so as not to injure the surrounding tissue.]
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, then you must make incisions around it so as to provide openings for drainage, but not so deep that they penetrate beyond the bone of the abscess; and above the point of each incision there should be a margin or a ring that prevents the point from penetrating beyond the bone. And you should have several such stoppers, placed in such a way as to cover the entire surface of the bone; this is the shape of the three types of stoppers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a drill on the bone, and turn it towards your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the drill a bit further, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the holes with the incisors, doing this as delicately and lightly as you can, until you draw out the bone with your hand or with one of the tools you have such as pincers; and take care not to touch the brain or the skull.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary to smooth the sharpness that remains of the bone with another tool similar to an incisor, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other incisors.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains any small bones or scales, remove them lightly with one of the tools; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is what Galen describes, which is safer and he praised it highly; and this is his statement:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. So that once you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lenticular scalpel, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not saw from one side, but rather make two cuts on either side so that the cutting edge faces the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet so that you lightly cut through the bone all around, taking great care of the cloth beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is attached to the bone, remove it carefully, for it can be removed without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the cloth, but rather it is only cut from above and there are small fragments, then you must smooth over that roughness and remove the splinters with a fine razor of which you should have various quantities, so as to make the most suitable adjustments according to the work and shape of the break in each location.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If the king before large razors, and afterward with finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	But the king (in every other haircut and fine breakage), it is necessary that you adjust according to its growth; and this is not an obvious matter even for one who has studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the abscess is exposed, then it is necessary to take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound, soak it in rose oil and place it on top of the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Next, take another cloth, doubled in two or three layers, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as gently as possible, taking care not to harm the abscess. Then apply a bandage over it without tightening too much, just enough to hold the wound closed.[0]
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess has subsided. Then loosen the bandage and apply medicinal herbs such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things. Make a powder of these ingredients and sprinkle it on the wound. Apply other mild medicines without causing biting pain.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And see that the wound is always clean, that you do not leave any pus, and do not allow any worms to gather, because when worms gather on the cloth of the brain, they will crawl and irritate, and this will cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on the siphac (a piece of bone in the skull), it will bite through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, if any bad accident should befall the patient, as we have said, it is to be doubted with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no other cause for the complication arises but from the medicine that has been applied, and it has such power, then you should take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and mix them with one cloth, and place it on the siphac (a piece of bone in the skull).
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the complication with various treatments until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, either one alone, as there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, it only swells or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or the hole of the nose, and align the break inside your index finger, and with your thumb on the outside, until the nose regains its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and your finger cannot reach it, then you should use a rod about as thick as a finger to align it.[References (in French)](https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k56390q/f76.item)
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, do the same and hurry to restore it on the first day if you can.[References (in French)](https://gallica.bnf.fr/ark:/12148/bpt6k56390q/f76.item)
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has calmed down, then apply to the wound of the broken part a linen cloth dipped in wine.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and put one (cloth) on the other side if the break is there; and let the bandages be so thick that they fill the wounds of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And some physicians say that one should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day. But it does not seem good to me; rather, they should be moistened with a preparation of egg yolk and powdered mill; then leave the bandage until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes goose feathers are put into the nose instead of bandages, and a soft cloth is wrapped around it, and the patient holds it in place, and breathes through it; do as you please.[ fight Club reference? :) ]
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the nose while you are working on it, put a wax seal or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a piece of diachylon (sticky plaster) on it.[Note: Diachylon is a medical term for a plaster that can be sticked to the skin and was used as a drug delivery system. It's like a medicated band-aid.]
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not appear, apply an external plaster, made of chamomile flour, and powdered incense, mixed with egg white, then put light wicks on it, but do not bind it.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture of the nail is small and it is broken into many pieces, then extract it with appropriate instruments, then sew up the wound, and cure it from harmful things such as dirt and pus, using appropriate plasters and ointments for this.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nail, then cure it with bandages and place splints of wood until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	about the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is only displaced, and not broken in two, except for a chip inside, it can be easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, you should insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture back into place, and align it with the other hand from the outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw fracture is separated into two parts, you must apply extension to both parts until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth or fractures occur, bind them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then apply a cerate to the broken jaw and place a double bandage over it. Place a large well-made star-shaped piece or a piece of leather of equal size, length, and width on top of the bandage, securing it as high as possible, and command the patient to rest and eat light foods.[Comments: The text recommends using precious metals such as gold or silver for binding fractured teeth, which is consistent with the medical practices of the time where expensive materials were often used in medical treatments. Cerate refers to a medicinal plaster or salve.]
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see the figure changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has become misaligned; and apply a plaster on top, with powder from the mill and plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and place light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not worsen, leave it on until it heals; it often heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, use what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, see if any piece of bone has been removed; it is necessary to delicately remove it with the appropriate instruments.[« »]
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as needed.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of suitable poultices for healing flesh until it has healed.
de la forcele	It is not clear how "de la forcele" fits into the previous text. If it is meant to be part of the translation, here are a few possibilities:
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break many times before, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated into two pieces, and this is the easiest to reset; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is when the fracture is without wound, to have two assistants, so that one holds the limb with the broken forceps; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then align the break between your hands, so that it is in its proper form, without any deformity or swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place below the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, and let it be thick according to your needs; and stretch and lift the forcemeat (a type of stuffing), and strain the sphere with your hand, so that you set the break evenly, as is necessary.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcemeat out of the casing because it has gone too deep, have the patient lie flat on his back, place a medium-sized pillow under his shoulder, and have the assistant push the shoulder downward until the bone of the forcemeat rises.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the break with your hands, and if you find it shattered, make an incision along the break; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, cut one of the incisions that you made; but place this instrument, the forcemeat, underneath to protect the wound.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and let it be shaped like a spoon, but not too narrow, and let it be as wide as is necessary, according to the size of the bone and the magnitude of the task; and let it have two openings, one large and one small, corresponding to the shape of the wound that you made when you pulled out the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are certain of a hot abscess, then cut the wound, and if the rupture is small, or if you doubt a hot abscess, then bandage the wound with linen cloths and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses appear, wet one linen cloth in rose oil, vinegar, and assyl, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and incisions, is to place on the bone an emplaster made of powdered molin and egg white, then place light bandages on top, and put a stick under the saddle, if you need one.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very large bandage of one palm in width, then place a double cloth on the bandages with emplaster, then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging.[5](https://www.medievalhealth.com/03%20Treatises%20-%20Surgery%20and%20Wounds/Anthony%20Flores.htm)
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stylet on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the neck, and under the healthy assellum, and under the diseased assellum; and manipulate each part, and when you see that the ligature holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stylet does not move above the broken bone, then reposition it every day, and when the ligature loosens, then tighten it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the affected side to raise the shoulder; this will lighten the fracture with the help of the alignment of the shoulder, where you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an adverse event occurs, for twenty days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	then reapply the plaster if necessary, and bind it in this way until they are healed; and it is healed in at most twenty-eight days, and sooner for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Not often does the shoulder break or dislocate to a noticeable extent, and it can only be detected through touch; prepare it according to the pattern of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form in every way possible; then put fine powder of the mill with plenty of egg, and light bandages, and place a double cloth over it; then place a wide and thin plate over it, a little larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate in any part of the shoulder, fill those hairs with linen bandages, so that the plate lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, making sure the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it softens, bind it again, and make sure the plate is in its place if it has moved, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is completed, unbind it, and be careful, for it is not an easy thing for the bone to come out of place.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone juts out and points above the knee, then cut it off and remove it, and do what we have said in the case of a fracture of the leg to calm a hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of a fractured rib.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	The pelvis is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the edge. And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and difficulty breathing, and may vomit blood, and the fracture can be seen clearly on the broken bone, and it can be felt.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back, and one places a cushion between the shoulders, then squeezes the shoulders, and brings together the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and subtly makes it even in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place poultices and compresses on top of the wound, made subtle with salt, or other light wood, and wrap it in a bandage, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around to the back, and tighten it appropriately, and check every hour if it has loosened, and if it has, then tighten it; and if it is necessary to unbind it, because of corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hurry, and unbind it, and remove the poultice, and treat what has come there with methods of cures; then remoisten the poultice, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures only come in thick areas after the back, and inside the chest, and they do not bend further except because they are slippery; and one can feel this well upon examination of the ribs.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the restoration is that you make even the fracture as it should be. And then apply a poultice and bind it with a splint if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is turning inward, then the patient feels intense pain, and swelling, as with pleurisy, for the bone pricks the skin; and the breath is punctured, and soon vomits a large quantity of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have put great skill into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say that one should administer foods that inflame the belly, to push the break outwards.[4](https://www.wileyhealth.com/content/reference/hbe/v_8207/i_15/c_16963)
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, because abscesses will not form if they have not already developed.[5](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1328074/)
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have already developed, then treat them.[8](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC2594072/)
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And said some of you that cupping glasses should be placed on the place, to strongly draw out (suction), and this seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the place due to the weakness (of the patient).
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you said that the place should be covered with a cloth soaked in hot oil, and tents are placed between the ribs to evenly pull the edges together, then it should be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pressing against the cloth, and the patient is in doubt, then it is necessary to make an incision on the place of the broken rib, and put a tool underneath to protect the lung; and then cut the bone, and gently pull, and then sew up the two edges of the wound if they are large, and treat it with poultices until it heals. And if abscesses come, then put on cloths soaked in rose oil, and place them on the place; and cure the place of what is necessary for an abscess, and lie down on the side where it is, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Here is the translation of the original Old French text you provided:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there occurs a fracture of the neck bones, and it rarely bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, pay attention if you see their hands weakened, swollen, and numb, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that they are mortally injured in many ways, but if they can move them and feel when they are strained and poked, know that the joints of the bone are safe, and that the patient will be cured if treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if a similar thing happens in the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, pay attention if their feet are weak, and if there are symptoms in their hands that are similar, and on their back there is a swelling and discharge without voluntary movement; and when it is pressed on their stomach, there is discharge without voluntary movement. And when they try to sit up while lying on their back, they cannot. Know that they are mortally injured: do not labor in their cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these symptoms do not occur, then the condition is less severe.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you should check if there is a hot abscess, and if there is, place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it calms down; then apply one of the healing and drying ointments, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain, until they are healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone gets dislocated, it should be covered on the chest; and remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then cure it with an ointment that draws out flesh, until it heals; and if the hole of the bone is broken, which is called the "hole of the cow", insert your left hand pocket, and place it evenly with your other hand to your power, then apply the ointment and bandage if necessary; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, push on it, remove it, and cure the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	"about the fracture of the thigh bone" (femur)
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the thigh bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is only slightly narrowed at the end; it bends long, and deviates to the side, causing pain to the patient in the area, swelling, and deformity of the fractured part.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it slopes inward, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that you can align the restoration of that break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice and place a wooden or bone splint on top, holding the break in place so that it does not move, and apply a bandage underneath the ribs, until they are properly aligned.[FAQ]
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses come in its place, do not touch it until the abscesses have calmed down, and apply what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and bind it as is necessary, if there is no adverse accident; and this is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the break of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is what is between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored in one of two ways: one of which is to take a rod of medium size, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two shoulders with two bandages and pull them up, and place the patient on a seat; then throw his broken arm over the rod, until it reaches the armpit and is in the middle of a bow-shaped piece of wood; then hang it over some heavy object or the attendant pulls it down; then put the surgeon's hands together around the break, until the break returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other manner is to place the patient on a stretcher, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold with one's hands what is above the break, and the other holds below all one tendon, and each pulls to their side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if you see that the extraction needs to be stronger, then tighten one tendon below the break, and above it, and have each assistant pull to their side. And if the break is close to the top of the shoulder, then you must place one tendon in the middle below the socket, and another towards the edge, below the break; and do the same if the break is toward the edge. Place a tendon lightly, without effort, just enough so that the break is aligned with its place, and the socket; then align the break as it should be, and tighten it, if there is no sign of abscesses.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess appears, then do not tighten it for seven days, and apply a wet linen cloth in vinegar and rose oil, until the abscess subsides; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening is that you put the poultice on the break, then place the arm on the shoulder or chest; and wrap the bandage, and tighten it on the stretcher, and on the arm, so that the arm remains straight, if nothing hinders it, or if the bone is not broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you are unsure whether the bone is broken, then use splints and place a wider and stronger splint over the break, with a space of two fingers between each splint, and make each splint large enough to pass over the break by three fingers on each side; then tighten it with splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter, more tightly and less evenly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you reset the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound up until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the binding every three days to see if itching, inflammation, or discharge comes to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. If so, loosen it as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not unbind it until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool underneath the affected area, and check every hour of the day and night to see that the shape of the broken member does not change, or if the binding has become too loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give them food as we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is initially fine; and when they begin to recover, the food should be coarse. It is customary for the affected area and leg to regain their normal state in 40 days; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and medicinal ointments to direct the place towards healing. And if the stricture is severe and embedded, then it should be left unbound for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	The text does not provide a new sentence in English, it just specifies that the previous instructions were about "the break of the arm" (la brisure du bras). Here is the previous translation again:
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "radius" and the "ulna," with one being smaller and the other being larger. The smaller one is located above, and it is the one that follows the thumb; while the larger one is located below, near the little finger. It may happen that only the large radius bone breaks, or only the small ulna bone, or both at once.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration and healing is easy; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when they are both broken together. If it is only the small bone that is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it is the large bone, then it must be stretched more forcefully; and it should be placed over a cushion, and the little finger of the hand should be held higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the others, and have the patient lie crosswise on it, with a cushion before them so that they do not suffer any labor. Then the assistant extends the patient's arm below at their side, or with a strap, and another assistant above. And then the doctor aligns it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the break is in pieces, then place each piece in its place, and if there is any piece that is torn and pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision above and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken of this in a separate chapter; then take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of the restoration pustules occur, then place a piece of lard cloth made of rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and gently bind a cloth over it, until the pustules have calmed down. And then remove the lard cloth, and apply the plaster of the powder from the mill with plenty of egg, then place the stylets, and let the stylet of the breakage be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches in several dispositions: whether the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more above the breakage than any other part, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is bound, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And wrap the member and the bandage after several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary to rinse the member with warm water until the itching has calmed down; and let the member not rest tightly. And then begin binding again, and if the bandages are softened and the bones disjoined, and similar things, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the blood flow cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you must loosen it slightly and leave it like that for several days until the blood flows again, and then bind it again.[x](https://www.memrise.com/learn/english/course/old-french/phrase/et-se-prend-warde-se-li-norrissemens-ne-puet-venir-au-member-por-ceu-quil-est-trop-estrois-si-covient-que-tu-lamollisses-i-poc-et-laisse-ensi-aucuns-jors-tant-que-li-norrissemens-i-corre-et-puis-lestrain/)
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have mentioned do not come to the patient, then do not release it until after 20 days or so; then let him wash his hands at his neck and let his neck be even, and watch for movement and swelling, and let him sleep on his back. And know that this breakage is restored in 30 or 35 days, and perhaps in 20 days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the broken hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that breaks in the back of the hand and at the knuckles often occur, but it is usually a sprain that happens many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, then the patient should sit cross-legged and sit upright in front of them; then place their hand on a spread out cloth, and the assistant straightens the broken bones and aligns them properly until they are well joined; and apply the dressing and bandages, unless there are abscesses, then place a splint according to the size of the location; and wrap it in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the break is on the outer side around the belly of the palm, then make a cushion of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken palm; and then bind it with a long bandage, and let the splint be made of wood as wide as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, then you should place a splint on top of it, and another underneath in the palm of the hand, so that the hand is open and straight; then bind it around the entire hand, and fasten the bandage between the fingers.[(\*](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/tout_entor) ")).
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the bone setter comes to one of our fingers, if it is crooked, place it evenly as it should be; and bind it with the sole (of a foot), and if you see fit, place a straight small stake to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, place it evenly, and bind it with the healthy finger that is after; or tie them all together, so that moving (the bandage) is useful, or place a stake on it, like on a crooked finger; and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and heal those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and it is easily visible when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends their ligature evenly to their part; and that is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the hip root, then let one of the ligaments be towards the wrist, and the other ligament below the fracture. And similarly if it is close to the knee, and then let the ligament be next to the knee, and let the extension be downwards; then let the surgeon place the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then put on the poultice and the bandage, if pus does not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down first and then return to your work and care; the ligature is done in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap over the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, leaving excess material; then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and let the end of the thread come to the top; then wrap back over the leg and thigh the bandage, then place splints on the fracture and one splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the gap between the thigh and the leg with soft cloths to make the tension even, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns over the fracture; and as you go further up from the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you put between the thigh and the leg, and tie three splints that are above, then go back down to the bottom end of the thread until you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, as long as there is no abscess or swelling or any other symptom.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a wound, untie it and treat what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that protrude, they should be removed if possible; and if not, then the wound must be opened wider and the fragments extracted; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, the patient does not fare well in such a restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored in 3 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that there are few fractures in the groove of the knee, but it often dislocates. And if it breaks, it is only a split or a hole, and this happens with all wounds, both with and without wounds, and this can be felt clearly.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you put evenly what is dislocated at its two ends, until it can be moved as a whole; then apply the poultice and place a round bandage if needed, and bind it appropriately. Then, consider all the precautions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar ones; and for each symptom, do what is necessary until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	Here is the translation of the first sentence you provided, without any comments or contextual information:
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that the leg has two bones, one of which is called by the proper name "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and there are all kinds of fractures in it just as in the arm, and therefore the restoration is identical to that of the arm, and the work is also the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns (i.e., becomes deformed) in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, set them straight again.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the large bones are broken, there is great pain and it is visible; set them right below (the skin). Then apply traction and align it evenly, and bind the ends of the bone evenly; but if the fracture is severe and there are multiple pieces, the traction should be less and lighter; and support according to its severity.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two straps of wooden sticks that encircle the leg on both sides, and they should be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap around it in two layers, one above and one below, and bind it evenly in the middle; with this binding, the leg will not be able to bend to the right or left; and some people use a wooden bar that encircles the leg to prevent movement, and it is properly done in cases of fracture where there is a wound; move the leg every day to check for redness, heat, or other symptoms; treat until it heals.
de la brisure des os dou piet	"Of the fracture of the bones of the foot" (or "in cases of broken foot bones")
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but sometimes there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and in the toes, and it only results in a crush injury in multiple ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bones of the foot and you see the bones protruding, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are protruding, and press it until they return to their place. Then apply a plaster and bandages, and place a small board with two flat surfaces under the affected foot, and bind it to the foot after wrapping the area with cloth and other necessary items.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding because you will find the bones aligned, whether they were broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.
